p. 11. Hilchos Bishul — Cooking
              Hilchos Bishul

1. What Constitutes Bishul

The Issur Doraisa: What Gets Cooked?
The Melacha of bishul (Av Melacha: cooking/baking - 'haofeh')
covers any significant transformation of food or material through
heat.
Authority            Position                       Notes / Key Point


Rambam (plain        No chiyuv doraisa for          Halacha does NOT
reading / R' Akiva   cooking food that is edible    follow this reading
Eiger)               raw - only for food that is
                     inedible raw


Mishnah              Chayav even for raw-edible     Still a minority position
Berurah's            food, if the cooking
reading of           improves it. Only excluded
Rambam               if there is no improvement
                     at all


Tosefos, Kol Bo,     Assur midoraisa to cook        This is the accepted
Riva, Ohr Zarua      raw food even if edible        halacha
                     beforehand - no distinction


Halacha              Assur midoraisa to cook
L'Maaseh             any food that is edible raw.
                     If cooking makes food
                     worse, may only be assur
                     miderabanan.
p. 21. Hilchos Bishul — Cooking
Yad Soledes Bo (YSB) - The Temperature Threshold
Bishul only takes effect at or above the temperature of Yad soledes
bo. Below this temperature there is no Torah prohibition. One may
not rely on one's own hand to test this - the assessment is
subjective and may differ from Talmudic times.


Authority          Position                    Notes / Key Point


Rav Moshe          Must be concerned from      Most stringent
Feinstein          43°C / ~109°F


Rav Bentsion       Must be concerned from      Most stringent
Abba Shaul         40°C / ~104°F


Rav Shlomo         YSB begins at 45°C /        Most lenient of the
Zalman Auerbach    ~113°F (based on goose      three
                   blood measurement)




Practical Rule:
Treat anything above 40°C (104°F) as potentially YSB. You cannot
test with your hand.
Common benchmark: food that you cannot hold in your closed hand
without discomfort is at or above YSB.


Maachal Ben Drussai (MB'D) - The 'Begun Cooking'
Threshold
A person is chayav for bishul once the food reaches the equivalent
of one-third cooked (Rashi) or one-half cooked (Rambam) - the
point at which a person would eat the food only in a time of great
need (b'shaas hadchak).
p. 31. Hilchos Bishul — Cooking
Practical implication: food that has reached MB'D on Shabbos
cannot be further cooked on Shabbos even to complete the cooking
- it has already triggered the issur.

Leaving Food Near Fire Where It Could Reach YSB
Scenario                          Halacha

Leaving uncooked liquid in a      FORBIDDEN miderabanan -
place where it can eventually     gezeira that one may forget and
reach YSB (even if intent is to   it will reach YSB (SA 318:14,
remove it first)                  Rash)


Leaving uncooked liquid in a      PERMITTED
place where it could NEVER
reach YSB


Leaving uncooked solid food       FORBIDDEN miderabanan -
where it could reach MB'D         same gezeira applies (Rama
                                  318:14)




2. Ein Bishul Achar Bishul - No
Recooking of Cooked Food

The Core Rule
Once food has been fully cooked, there is no issur doraisa to cook it
again in the same medium. This is the principle of 'Ein bishul achar
bishul' (EBA'B).
p. 41. Hilchos Bishul — Cooking
Dvar Yavesh (Dry Solid Food) - Simple Case
Food Type / Scenario                  Halacha

Dry, fully cooked solid food -        PERMITTED midoraisa - EBA'B
reheating on Shabbos                  applies. Effect of cooking never
                                      disappears from dry food.

placing near the fire where it will   Re'eim's concern about tsli only

                                      taam tsli)


Dry solid food - placed on            Assur - this is tsli achar bishul;

roasted/toasted (taam tsli)           significant




Dvar Lach (Liquid / Cooked Liquid) - Bishul Achar
Bishul
Liquids are fundamentally different: if a cooked liquid cools down,
the question is whether the effect of cooking 'disappears,' triggering
a new issur bishul when reheated.

p. 61. Hilchos Bishul — Cooking
Practical Summary - Reheating Liquids (Ashkenaz):
Hot soup / tea / coffee that is still hot (above eating temperature):
PERMITTED to reheat.
Warm soup that is below eating temperature: FORBIDDEN (Shulchan
Aruch HaRav / Rav Moshe / Rav Berkovits).
Soup that has completely cooled to room temperature: FORBIDDEN -
all agree (though Rav Berkovits: it is a chumra, not doraisa).
Sefardim: follow Mechaber who holds like Rashi - once below YSB it
is assur.

Molid - Changing the Form of a Solid
A separate issur derabanan: causing a solid to turn into a liquid
form (e.g. melting ice into an empty cup, melting butter onto an
empty plate). This is Molid - creating a 'new' form.
Scenario                             Halacha

Melting ice or butter into an        FORBIDDEN - Molid (issur
empty cup or plate                   derabanan)


Melting ice into a cup of water      PERMITTED - not considered
(melts into existing liquid)         Molid since it dissolves into the
                                     existing liquid


Melting butter onto a hot piece of   PERMITTED - absorbed into the
food                                 solid food, not forming a puddle
                                     (Rav Moshe)
p. 81. Hilchos Bishul — Cooking
3. Bishul Achar Tsli / Tsli Achar Bishul

Background: Types of Cooking
Bishul = cooking in liquid. Tsli = roasting over open fire. Afiyah =
baking in oven (treated like tsli). Deep-frying = bishul. Shallow-frying
= tsli.
Authority           Position                         Notes / Key Point


Re'eim (Hagahos     There IS bishul achar tsli -     Ashkenaz is strict for
Maimones)           assur to cook something          this
                    previously baked/roasted.
                    Even in a Kli sheini (bread),
                    since bread is kalei habishul.

(Mordechai)         cook something previously
                    baked.

                    she'omer' and Ravya as           Ben Ish Chai and Rav

                    Ravya, but advisable to be       Ovadia lenient
                    strict

                    Ashkenazim do not cook           practice
                    previously baked food. Even
                    Kli sheini forbidden for bread
                    (kalei habishul).


Chazon Ish          Re'eim only forbids when         Key leniency for
                    there is actual 'taam tsli'      hotplate/blech
                    (flavor of roasting). Merely
                    warming cooked food by fire
                    does not create taam tsli.

p. 131. Hilchos Bishul — Cooking
5. Kli Rishon, Kli Sheini, and Kli Shlishi

Definitions and Status
Kli Rishon (KR): The vessel in which food was cooked on the fire.
Its walls retain heat and can continue to cook food even off the fire -
its cooking status is DORAISA even off the fire.
Irui Kli Rishon: Pouring from a KR onto food. Cooks a klipa (outer
layer) of dry food - treated as Kli sheini for most purposes. Into
liquid: see below.
Kli Sheini (KS): A vessel into which hot food/liquid has been poured
from a KR. Its walls have cooled the liquid - does not cook
midoraisa (in most cases). Raw food may be placed in it (with
exceptions - see below).
Kli Shlishi (KSH): A vessel into which food has been poured from a
KS. Generally no concern at all. Rav Auerbach: kalei habishul
forbidden even in a KSH (midoraisa). Rav Moshe / Chazon Ish /
Rav Berkovits: permitted.



Kli Rishon - Off the Fire: Does It Still Cook?

Halacha:
A Kli Rishon that is off the fire can still cook midoraisa as long as it is
above YSB.
Therefore: do not add raw uncooked ingredients to a Kli Rishon even
off the fire if it is YSB.




Irui Kli Rishon Into Liquids

midoraisa.

6. Dvar Gush and the Ladle

Dvar Gush - Status of a Hot Piece of Solid Food
When a hot solid piece of food (dvar gush) is removed from a Kli
Rishon and placed in a Kli Sheini - does it remain a Kli Rishon (and
can it cook other food) or does it become a Kli Sheini?

7. Cooking in the Sun (Toldos Chama)
and Other Heat Sources
Heat Source / Scenario               Halacha

Cooking directly in the sun (e.g.    PERMITTED - the sun itself is not
egg in direct sunlight)              a form of fire (SA 318:3)


Cooking using an object heated       FORBIDDEN miderabanan -
by the sun (Toldos Chama - e.g.      gezeira to protect from Toldos
kerchief heated in sun)              Ohr (objects heated by fire)


Cooking using Toldos Ohr -           FORBIDDEN - same as cooking
objects heated by fire (e.g. a hot   on fire itself
pot next to the fire)


Placing food on a hotplate/blech     PERMITTED - the blech itself was
already on from before Shabbos       heated before Shabbos. Issue of

                                     Berurah: only issur if metal
                                     actually softens.

p. 261. Hilchos Bishul — Cooking
Quick Summary: Core Principles
The 10 Most Important Rules of Hilchos Bishul:
1. BISHUL APPLIES TO ALL FOOD: Assur midoraisa to cook any
food - even if edible raw - if cooking improves it.
2. YSB THRESHOLD: Treat anything above 40°C as potentially YSB.
Cannot test with your hand.
3. EIN BISHUL ACHAR BISHUL - DRY FOOD: Once dry food is fully
cooked, may reheat freely (no EBA'B).
4. EIN BISHUL ACHAR BISHUL - LIQUID: Once liquid cools to below
eating temperature, forbidden to reheat (Ashkenaz: Shulchan Aruch
HaRav / Rav Moshe / Rav Berkovits). Remove from heat if it dropped
below this point.
5. BISHUL ACHAR TSLI: Ashkenazim: do not cook previously
baked/roasted food. Kli Sheini or Kli Rishon - forbidden for bread.
Solution: use Kli Shlishi.
6. KLI RISHON OFF FIRE: Still cooks midoraisa if YSB. Do not add
raw food.
7. KLI SHEINI: Mutar to put water, oil, salt, whole spices. Forbidden:
bread, eggs, tea (kalei habishul), ground spices (Rav Auerbach / Rav
Berkovits), most other raw foods (Magen Avraham / Mishnah
Berurah).
8. KLI SHLISHI: Generally permitted for everything. Exceptions:
teabag (Rav Auerbach), but Rav Moshe / Rav Berkovits lenient.
9. DVAR GUSH: Treat hot pieces of food as Kli Rishon (Mishnah
Berurah / Ashkenaz stringency). Exception: surrounded by gravy (half
covered) = Kli Sheini. Combine with ladle = Kli Shlishi in plate.
10. LADLE: If pot was off fire - ladle is always Kli Sheini; plate = Kli
Shlishi (Chazon Ish / Rav Berkovits). This makes most Shabbos table
scenarios more manageable.
p. 272. Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara
                     Hilchos Shabbos
                 Hatmana, Shehiya, and Chazara

 1. Hatmana - Insulating a Pot
Hatmana is the Rabbinic prohibition of surrounding a pot to retain or add
heat. There are two categories: (a) Dvar hamosif hevel - a covering that
actively adds its own heat; (b) Dvar she'eino mosif hevel - a covering that
merely retains heat.

Basic Rules - When Is Hatmana Permitted?

Scenario                           Halacha


Dvar hamosif hevel (adds heat)     FORBIDDEN - even on Erev Shabbos.
- Erev Shabbos                     Gezeira lest one insulate with live
                                   embers (remetz) and come to stoke
                                   on Shabbos.


Dvar hamosif hevel - during        FORBIDDEN (per Mechaber / Rashi's
Bein Hashmashos                    girsa). Permitted only per
                                   Rif/Rambam's girsa - rejected by most
                                   Rishonim.


Dvar hamosif hevel - on            FORBIDDEN
Shabbos itself


Dvar she'eino mosif hevel - Erev   PERMITTED
Shabbos


Dvar she'eino mosif hevel -        PERMITTED - food is still hot so no
during Bein Hashmashos             concern of stoking


Dvar she'eino mosif hevel - on     FORBIDDEN - gezeira lest one see
Shabbos                            food cooled and come to reheat it
                                   (Rashi)

 2. Shehiya - Leaving Food on the Fire
Shehiya is the Rabbinic prohibition of leaving food on an open fire as
Shabbos begins, lest one come to stoke the fire on Shabbos (shema
yechateh). Two ways around it exist: grufa (removing coals) and ketuma
(covering coals with ash).

The Core Machlokes: Chachamim vs. Chanania

Authority        Position                        Notes / Key Point


Chanania         Permitted to leave food on      Mb'd = 1/3 cooked
                 open fire if it has reached     (Rashi); 1/2 cooked
                 Maachal Ben Drussai (Mb'd)      (Rambam). Minhag
                 by the time Shabbos enters.
p. 332. Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara
Authority       Position                       Notes / Key Point


                No concern of stoking once     follows Chanania.
                the food is at Mb'd.


Chachamim       Forbidden to leave food on     Rif / Rambam follow this.
                open fire even if Mb'd. Only   Mechaber brings as
                permitted if food is fully     primary opinion.
                cooked AND mistamek v'rah
                lo (getting worse). [Per Rav
                and Shmuel's reading.]


Rosh            Agrees with Chachamim in       Machlokes between MB
                principle but concludes        and Chazon Ish on what
                minhag was like Chanania.      the Rosh meant.
                'Yisrael should be left to
                keep their minhagim.'


Mishnah         The minhag of leniency         In a makom tsorech, rely
Berurah         (Chanania) is not ideal; one   on Chanania.
                should l'chatchila be strict
                like Chachamim.


Chazon Ish      The Rosh's leniency is fully   Rav Berkovits: rules like
                lechatchila - the minhag is    Mishnah Berurah.
                legitimate and connected to
                oneg Shabbos.




HALACHA L'MAASEH - Shehiya: Ashkenazim: Minhag is like Chanania
(lenient). Ideally reach Mb'd by shkia. In makom tsorech, rely on
Chanania even without grufa/ketuma. Rav Berkovits: l'chatchila do
grufa/ketuma. | Sefardim: Also have minhag to follow Chanania.
p. 342. Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara
Status of Modern Cooking Utensils

Scenario                       Halacha


Platta (hot plate, no knobs)   Most Poskim: considered garuf v'katum
                               - may leave any food on it as Shabbos
                               enters. Rav Elyashiv: NOT garuf
                               v'katum; must cover with thick layer of
                               foil (or two thin layers). Rav Berkovits:
                               follows majority - platta is garuf
                               v'katum.


Gas stovetop (with knobs)      NOT garuf v'katum - raising gas is like
                               adding wood. To make katum: cover the
                               flame AND the knobs (Rav Feinstein).
                               Rav Aaron Kotler: cover knobs only.
                               Standard practice: use a blech.


Blech covering stovetop        Blech = garuf v'katum - may leave food
                               on stovetop. Ensure blech covers the
                               knobs too. If knobs not covered, cover
                               them separately.


Electric oven                  To make katum: place metal box inside
                               covering elements, OR cover elements
                               with foil. Also cover the buttons/knobs.
                               Rav Berkovits rules this way.


Crockpot / slow cooker         Treated like open fire for shehiya. To
                               use: food must be Mb'd by Shabbos
                               (Chanania), OR perform equivalent of
                               ketuma on the dial.


Urn / hot water urn            Treated like open fire for shehiya. Most
                               urns have no way to raise the heat -
                               status may be like garuf v'katum. Ask a
                               posek for your specific model.

 3. Chazara - Returning a Pot to the Fire
Chazara is the prohibition of returning a pot to a fire on Shabbos. It is
stricter than shehiya - it requires grufa u'ketuma even according to
Chanania. Beis Hillel permits chazara with conditions; Beis Shammai
forbids it entirely. Halacha follows Beis Hillel.

Conditions Required for Chazara (Tanai Chazara)
Three possible conditions are discussed in the Gemara: (1) Odan beyado -
pot remained in his hand; (2) Daato lehachzir - intended to return it when
p. 392. Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara
he took it off; (3) Lo hiniach al gabei karka - did not put the pot on the
ground.

Chananel)          Putting pot on the ground =     Gemara questions.

                   or daato lehachzir.

                   permitted if had daato

                   cooled)




Liquid food (with gravy etc.): must be above YSB to return (Mechaber)
or have some warmth (Rama). Dry food: must have some warmth
(Magen Avraham / Rav Feinstein). In makom tsorech for dry food: Gra

is lenient even if fully cooled.

                   applies on Shabbos itself


Tosefos /          Forbidden to place pot on         They disagree on how
Rosh / Smag        fire so close to Shabbos that,    cooked food must be:
                   if the food were cold, it could   see below
                   not heat up before Shabbos.
                   Applies even to currently hot
                   food.


Rosh               Issur chazara on Erev
                   Shabbos only if food is
                   FULLY COOKED (since then
                   there's no bishul concern to
                   override the chazara
                   concern)
p. 432. Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara
Authority         Position                        Notes / Key Point


Tosefos           Issur applies once food has
                  reached Mb'd


Smag              Issur always applies unless
                  food is totally raw (lo plug)


Rama              Minhag is lenient, but good     Mishnah Berurah: like
                  to be strict when there is no   Rosh - only fully cooked
                  great need                      triggers the issur. Adds
                                                  chumra of Smag.



Workaround (Rav Auerbach): First put pot on high flame (where food will
be ready by Shabbos), then lower the flame. Chazon Ish / Rav Kanievsky:
not needed - since one could raise the flame, the issur doesn't apply even
on a low flame.

Quick Summary: Core Rules at a Glance
#   Rule                             Key Point


1   Dvar hamosif hevel               FORBIDDEN Erev Shabbos, Bein
                                     Hashmashos, and Shabbos. No
                                     exceptions.


2   Dvar she'eino mosif hevel        Permitted Erev Shabbos and Bein
                                     Hashmashos. Forbidden on
                                     Shabbos itself (unless already
                                     covered before Shabbos).


3   Covering/insulating pot          Permitted to replace, switch, or
    already covered before           add a cover even on Shabbos - as
    Shabbos                          long as food is fully cooked.


4   Shehiya - minhag                 Both Ashkenazim and Sefardim
                                     follow Chanania: leave food on
                                     fire if it reached Mb'd (1/3–1/2
                                     cooked) by shekia. L'chatchila:
                                     perform grufa/ketuma.


5   Platta = garuf v'katum           Most Poskim: platta is garuf
                                     v'katum; may leave any food. Rav
                                     Berkovits: l'chatchila cover with
                                     foil. Rav Elyashiv: must cover.


6   Blech on stovetop                Blech = garuf v'katum. Must also
                                     cover knobs.


7   Chazara requires grufa/ketuma    Cannot return a pot to an open
                                     fire without grufa/ketuma - even
                                     with all other conditions met.


8   Tanai chazara (Ashkenaz)         Requires: (a) not put on ground,
                                     (b) odan beyado, (c) daato
                                     lehachzir. In makom tsorech: one
p. 472. Hatmana, Shehiya & Chazara
#    Rule                                Key Point


                                         condition is sufficient. Rav
                                         Berkovits: lenient with
                                         combinations.


9    Pot put on ground with daato        Shaas hadchak: consult a rav
     lehachzir                           (Orchos Shabbos) or be lenient
                                         combining Yerushalmi (Rav
                                         Berkovits).


10   Food must have some warmth          Fully cold dry food: b'makom
     for chazara                         tsorech permitted (Gra). Liquid:
                                         must be YSB (Mechaber).
                                         Ashkenaz: any warmth is
                                         sufficient.

agrees.

8. Planting a Seed on Shabbos - Why the Stricter
Penalty?
The Mishna (Terumos 2:3): if one plants a seed on Shabbos b'meizid - must uproot
it forever (per Rebbe Meir). Per Rebbe Yehuda: even b'shogeg must uproot. This
is stricter than bishul. The Acharonim offer four explanations:

   Authority        Reason for Strict Penalty         Implication for Other
                                                            Melachos


Tosefos Yom       When possible to reverse         Any reversible Melacha (e.g.
Tov + Tiferes     the Melacha, one must do         building) must also be
Yisrael           so. Cooking cannot be            undone
                  reversed; planting can.


Mishna            Penalty must prevent the         Building (for future use) =
Rishonah          sinner from achieving his        must destroy. Clothing /
                  intent. For cooking: intent is   paintings = must destroy.
                  that day - forbidding on
                  Shabbos suffices. For
                  planting: intent is future
                  growth - only uprooting
                  prevents achievement.


Kehillas          Unique to planting: growth       Building: no ongoing post-
Yaakov            continues after Shabbos due      Shabbos effect - no need to
(Steipler)        to the Shabbos Melacha, so       destroy.
                  benefit continues
                  perpetually.


Biur Halacha      Penalty can only work when       Building completed on
                  the benefit is available on      Shabbos: benefit is on
                  Shabbos itself. Planted          Shabbos - no need to
                  seed: no benefit on Shabbos
p. 563. Maaseh Shabbos
                     - so Chazal forbade benefit       destroy.
                     forever.


⚑ Practical: If Jews build a house on Shabbos - most Acharonim hold
forbidden to live there ever. Painting / clothing made on Shabbos by a
meizid = forbidden to buy. Shogeg + shaas hadchak: may be lenient with
kedai sheyaasu.

p. 624. Amira L'Akum
                Amira L'Akum

1. Foundations

Status of the Prohibition
Amira l'akum is an issur miderabanan according to the consensus
of the Rishonim. The verse in Shemos 12:16 is used merely as an
asmachta (Ramban).
Three Reasons

Zara 15a)         about melacha on Shabbos        explicit speech on

                  Yeshaya)


Rashi (Shabbos    Shlichus - non-Jew acts as      Applies when non-Jew
153a)             the Jew's agent; treated as     acts as the Jew's agent
                  if the Jew did it himself


Rambam            Shabbos will become 'light      Basis for Rav Moshe's
(Shabbos 6:1)     in one's eyes' if Jews freely   prohibition of time-

Scenario                            Halacha L'Maaseh

Bottom Line:
The halacha is l'chumra for all three reasons. All the above scenarios
are forbidden unless a specific heter applies.
p. 644. Amira L'Akum

Issur Derabanan for a Mitzva - Shvus D'Shvus
The key heter: asking a non-Jew (itself a shvus) to do an issur
derabanan (also a shvus) = shvus d'shvus, which Chazal treated
more leniently.


Authority            Position                      Notes


Rambam               Permitted to ask non-Jew      The main relied-upon
(Shabbos 6:9)        to do issur derabanan for     position
                     any mitzva, great need, or
                     miksas choli


Ramban               Only permitted for the sake
                     of bris milah - not other
                     mitzvos


Mechaber (SA         Rules like the Rambam -       Practical halacha
307:5)               permitted for mitzva, great   follows this
                     need, or miksas choli




Practical Halacha:
Asking a non-Jew to do an issur derabanan is permitted for a mitzva,
in a time of great need, or for miksas choli (Rambam / Mechaber).
For a melacha doraisa - generally strict, except: (a) fixing an Eiruv
(Mishnah Berurah), (b) mitzva d'rabbim (Rav Moshe).
p. 674. Amira L'Akum

Important Note:
Even when hinting is permitted, the Jew must be able to benefit from
the resulting melacha.
If the non-Jew does a positive melacha for the Jew (e.g. turns on a
light in a dark room), the Jew may not benefit regardless - so hinting
achieves nothing.
Hinting is effective only where benefit would in any case be permitted:
e.g. turning off a light, or adding light to an already-lit room.
p. 714. Amira L'Akum

p. 734. Amira L'Akum
Authority            Position                       Notes


                     even in Jew's home

                     unless non-Jew adds a

                     on light in dark room)




Practical Rule:
Non-Jew turns on light in dark room for a Jew - Jew MUST protest.
Non-Jew turns off a light, or adds light where there is already some
light - minhag is no protest required.
If the Jew protested and non-Jew ignored him - Jew may benefit.
p. 744. Amira L'Akum
7. When the Jew Could Have Done It
Himself (Rabbeinu Tam)
The Machlokes
Rabbeinu Tam: If the Jew could have obtained the benefit himself
without the non-Jew's melacha, it is permitted to benefit even when
the non-Jew did it for the Jew. (Example: a man can drink from the
well himself - so when the non-Jew draws water for him, it is
permitted.)
Ri, Rosh, Ran, Rambam: Forbidden regardless - benefiting from a
non-Jew's melacha done for a Jew is always forbidden.



Halacha L'Maaseh
Scenario                         Halacha L'Maaseh

Non-Jew carries food through a   FORBIDDEN - basic halacha
reshus harabim for the Jew       follows the Ri

carmelis (issur derabanan) -     time of great need: may even ask
significant Shabbos need         l'chatchila (Mishnah Berurah)


Non-Jew carries food through a   FORBIDDEN
carmelis - no particular need


Asking non-Jew to move muktza    PERMITTED - Jew could have
that is in the way (Jew could    moved it himself via tiltul min
move it via tiltul min hatzad)   hatzad (Rama 276:3)


Asking non-Jew to move muktza    FORBIDDEN - Jew could not
to protect the muktza            have moved it himself for that

p. 754. Amira L'Akum

8. Gezeira: Shema Yarbeh Bishvilo

The Rule
Even when a non-Jew does melacha for himself, Chazal forbade a
Jew from benefiting when there is concern that the non-Jew will add
to the melacha for the Jew's sake - if the non-Jew knows the Jew.

p. 804. Amira L'Akum
Summary: Key Practical Principles
Core Rules at a Glance:
1. Amira l'akum is assur miderabanan - all three reasons (Daber
Davar, Shlichus, Rambam) apply l'chumra.
2. Asking a non-Jew to do an issur derabanan is permitted for a
mitzva, great need, or miksas choli (Rambam / Mechaber - SA 307:5).
3. Asking for a melacha doraisa for a mitzva: generally strict.
Exceptions: fixing an Eiruv (Mishnah Berurah); mitzva d'rabbim (Rav
Moshe).
4. Benefiting from non-Jew's melacha: positive benefit forbidden;
removing a nuisance (negative benefit) permitted.
5. Adding light to an already-lit room: permitted. Turning on light in a
dark room: forbidden.
6. When non-Jew is paid: Mechaber lenient, Rama strict.
7. Hinting: only indirect comments with no command and no mention
of melacha are permitted.
8. Amira l'amira (asking non-Jew to tell another non-Jew): lenient only
in great loss; no positive benefit.
9. Time-switches: permitted - all Poskim except Rav Moshe.
10. Psik reisha: Rama is lenient for amira l'akum; Mishnah Berurah
lenient for de'lo nichah leih in Shabbos need.
p. 815. Amira L'Yisrael
             Amira L'Yisrael

2. Asking a Jew Who Holds a Lenient
Opinion

The Core Issue
May a Jew who follows a strict ruling ask a Jew who follows a
lenient ruling to do the melacha for him? Two potential problems:
(1) Daber Davar - asking someone to do what you hold is forbidden.
(2) Lifnei Iver - placing a stumbling block before another Jew.

Rav Auerbach's Ruling (Minchas Shlomo 2:35)
If a Jew is strict only because of his Rabbi's ruling or community
minhag - not because he personally concluded the halacha is strict
- he does not believe the other person is doing an issur. Therefore
there is no Lifnei Iver and no Daber Davar, and he may ask the
lenient Jew to do the melacha.
If the Jew personally investigated the sugya and concluded
l'halacha that the strict view is correct, he may NOT ask the lenient
Jew - he considers the other to be doing an issur.



Practical Cases
Scenario                           Halacha L'Maaseh

Sefardi (follows Mechaber:         Rav Auerbach: PERMITTED if
forbidden to reheat warm liquid)   Sefardi has not personally
asks Ashkenazi (follows Rama:      investigated and holds it as issur
permitted) to reheat liquid        - he just follows his Rav. Rav
                                   Berkovits rules this way.


Jew personally holds the strict    FORBIDDEN - he believes the
view after learning the sugya -    other is doing an issur (Rav
asks lenient Jew to do melacha     Auerbach; Rav Wosner strict in
p. 855. Amira L'Yisrael
Scenario                             Halacha L'Maaseh

                                     any case)


Jew strict for Rabbeinu Tam only     Rav Auerbach / Rav Berkovits:
as his Rav's ruling - asks           PERMITTED. Rav Wosner:
someone not keeping Rabbeinu         FORBIDDEN.
Tam to do melacha before
Rabbeinu Tam's zman




Bottom Line:
Rav Berkovits rules like Rav Auerbach: if one is strict only due to
minhag or one's Rav, one may ask a lenient Jew.
Most other Poskim (including Rav Wosner) are strict.

4. Business on Shabbos and Schar
Shabbos
Doing Business on Shabbos
It is assur miderabanan to conduct business on Shabbos - a
gezeira to prevent a Jew from coming to write on Shabbos.
Borrowing and lending items is permitted.
Rebbe Akiva Eiger: Forbidden to make an acquisition on Erev
Shabbos that takes effect on Shabbos (e.g. mechiras chametz
when Erev Pesach falls on Shabbos). Ksav Sofer and Maharam
Shick agree; Maharsham disagrees. Poskim are generally
concerned for Rebbe Akiva Eiger's view.



The Drinks Machine / Online Business - Two Issues
Authority          Position                       Notes


Orchos Shabbos     Lenient re: Rebbe Akiva
                   Eiger - he only forbade an
                   explicit condition that
                   acquisition takes place on
                   Shabbos; a machine
                   involves no such words or
                   act. Logic applies to online
                   business too (but consult a
                   posek for specific
                   situations).


Minchas Yitzchak   Lenient with four
                   conditions: (1) machine not
                   on Jew's property; (2) not
                   publicly known to be the
                   Jew's; (3) owner intends to
                   transfer ownership to buyer
                   on Erev Shabbos; (4)
                   owner intends not to
p. 885. Amira L'Yisrael
Authority            Position                      Notes


                     acquire payment until after
                     Shabbos.


Rav Wosner           FORBIDDEN - constitutes
                     Schar Shabbos




Schar Shabbos - Earning Money on Shabbos
It is rabbinically forbidden to be paid specifically for work done only
on Shabbos (a gezeira to protect other business prohibitions).
Paying a non-Jewish worker for Shabbos work is permitted - the
issur applies to the one being paid.

The Three Heterim for Schar Shabbos
Scenario                             Halacha L'Maaseh

Havlaah - worker is hired for the    PERMITTED - the most common
week (not Shabbos alone); pay        heter. Also applies to a Baal
for Shabbos is 'absorbed' into       Korei paid for his weekly
the weekly wage                      preparation + leining.


Matanah - employer designates        PERMITTED - used for
the payment as a gift, not wages     babysitters who work only on
(worker must genuinely accept        Shabbos. Note: morally
this)                                questionable to rely on this
                                     routinely.


L'tzorech Mitzva - Chazzan, Baal     Mechaber 306:5 brings two
Korei, etc.                          opinions. Mishnah Berurah: one
                                     who relies on leniency 'will not
                                     see blessing from his work on
                                     Shabbos.'
p. 895. Amira L'Yisrael

               apply to interest payments
               - permitted

Feinstein      apply in principle.            disputed day's accrual

               Shabbos runs night to day

               an issue when Shabbos is
               sandwiched between two
               days of Yom Tov.
p. 905. Amira L'Yisrael
5. Amira L'Kattan - Asking a Child to Do
Melacha

Background: Is Beis Din Obligated to Stop a Child
from Sinning?
There is a machlokes Amoraim (Yevamos 113b-114a) whether Beis
Din must prevent a child from doing an issur doraisa. All agree: Beis
Din need NOT prevent a child from doing an issur derabanan.


Authority          Position


Rashba             Beis Din is NOT obligated to prevent a child from
                   doing issurei doraisa


Tosefos            Every adult is obligated to stop a child above the age
                   of chinuch from sinning (doraisa and derabanan)


Rambam             Adults are not obligated; only the father is obligated to
                   stop his own child (because of chinuch)


Mechaber (343:1)   Rules like the Rambam - adults not obligated to stop
                   other people's children


Rama (343:1)       Brings Tosefos - adults are obligated for children
                   above chinuch age


Chayei Adam /      Everyone obligated for issur doraisa; only father
Mishnah Berurah    obligated for issur derabanan
p. 915. Amira L'Yisrael
Causing a Child to Do an Issur Doraisa
Scenario                              Halacha L'Maaseh

Actively causing a child of any       FORBIDDEN - two issurim:
age to do an issur doraisa            general prohibition + 'Atah
                                      u'vincha' (specific to Shabbos,
                                      from the Torah's verse)


Putting a very young child near a     Some Poskim lenient (not a
light switch knowing he may turn      direct command). Many Gedolim
it on                                 strongly oppose this leniency -
                                      only use in rare, significant need.



Causing a Child to Do an Issur Derabanan

Rambam /             FORBIDDEN to cause a
Mechaber             child to do an issur
                     derabanan in all
                     circumstances


Rashba / Ran         Permitted if it is for the
                     BENEFIT OF THE CHILD

                     if the child uses the siddur -
                     father may then use it too

below age of chinuch                   (all agree)

above age of chinuch                   Mechaber - not obligated;
                                       Rama/Tosefos - obligated for
                                       doraisa; Mishnah Berurah:
                                       obligated for doraisa only.

must stop him                          request


Asking child to do a psik reisha       PERMITTED (Rav Auerbach, Rav

p. 935. Amira L'Yisrael
Key Distinctions at a Glance:
Issur doraisa - forbidden to cause a child in all cases. No exceptions.
Issur derabanan - forbidden per Mechaber; permitted for child's own
benefit per Rashba (relied upon in time of need).
Psik reisha where child is unaware - permitted (Rav Auerbach et al.).
The obligation to stop a sinning child rests primarily on the father;
other adults obligated for doraisa (Mishnah Berurah).



Summary: Key Practical Principles
Core Rules at a Glance:
1. Erev Shabbos: One who accepted Shabbos may ask one who has
not to do melacha - permitted (Rashba, Mechaber, Rama).
2. Motsei Shabbos: One who has not yet taken out Shabbos may ask
one who has - permitted (Rama; Levush is strict).
3. Exception: If the person is strict due to halachic concern that it is
actually Shabbos/Yom Tov - FORBIDDEN.
4. Following a different posek: If strict only due to minhag/Rav (not
personal conviction) - may ask a lenient Jew (Rav Auerbach / Rav
Berkovits).
5. Ben chutz l'aretz in Israel on Yom Tov Sheini: Issur doraisa -
forbidden. Issur derabanan for need/mitzva - permitted (Rav
Berkovits, following Rav Moshe).
6. Schar Shabbos: Forbidden to be paid for Shabbos-only work.
Heterim: havlaah (most common), matanah, possibly l'tzorech mitzva.
7. Interest: Rav Auerbach - no issur. Rav Moshe - issur in principle;
practically only an issue when Shabbos is sandwiched by two Yom
Tov days.
8. Causing a child to do issur doraisa - forbidden in all cases.
9. Causing a child to do issur derabanan for child's benefit - permitted
(Rashba; relied upon).
10. Psik reisha via a child who is unaware - permitted (Rav Auerbach
et al.).
p. 946. Kavannah U'Maaseh
                  Kavannah U'Maaseh


1. Missasek
Missasek: A person intends to do one action but accidentally does a
different forbidden action. He did not plan to do the forbidden act at all.
Distinct from shogeg (knew the act, not the issur).

Two Types (Tosefos, Sanhedrin 62b)
Type                                     Status


Missasek She'naaseh                      Rav: patur from korban only; still
Machshavto His intent was                transgresses issur doraisa (Rebbe
partially fulfilled (e.g. reached for    Akiva Eiger) Nesivos / Rav Chaim
this vegetable - grabbed the same        Soloveitchik: not issur doraisa
vegetable, but it was attached)


Missasek She'lo Naaseh                   Patur from korban AND from issur
Machshavto His intent was not            doraisa Still assur miderabanan
fulfilled at all (e.g. cut a             (Rebbe Akiva Eiger)
completely different vegetable)



Source for Exemption
Source                                   Applies To


Verse: 'It must become known to          She'naaseh Machshavto -
him' (Vayikra 4:23)                      exempts from korban only


Meleches Machsheves (intent              She'lo Naaseh Machshavto -
required)                                exempts from issur doraisa
                                         entirely
p. 956. Kavannah U'Maaseh
Practical Applications: (1) Obligated to stop someone else about to
do a melacha b'missasek (e.g., opening a fridge not knowing the
light is on). (2) Take precautions - check pockets before Shabbos
to avoid carrying b'missasek (Shulchan Aruch 252:7).



2. Dvar She'eino Miskavein & Psik Reisha
Dvar She'eino Miskavein: A permitted act that may (but not necessarily
will) cause a forbidden act. Machlokes Tanaim - halacha follows Rebbe
Shimon (permitted).


Category                Definition                Status


Dvar She'eino           Permitted act that        MUTAR - halacha
Miskavein               may cause a               follows Rebbe
                        forbidden result (not     Shimon (SA 337:1)
                        certain)

De'nichah Leih          certainly cause a
                        forbidden result;
                        person is glad for the
                        result


Psik Reisha De'lo       Certainly causes          Assur miderabanan
Nichah Leih             forbidden result;         (Tosefos / Mechaber).
                        person does NOT           Aruch: mutar. When
                        care                      combined with other
                                                  leniencies, may be
                                                  permitted.

4. Melacha She'ein Sricha Legufa
Melacha She'ein Sricha Legufa: Person intends to do the melacha, but not
for the same purpose it was done in the Mishkan / not for a constructive
benefit. Machlokes Rishonim on the definition and status.

Definition - Two Opinions
Rashi                                 Tosefos


Done merely to remove something       Done for a different purpose than
from one's way, not to accomplish     the melacha served in the
a positive goal                       Mishkan

                          She'ein Sricha
                          Legufa


Rambam (rules like        ASSUR MIDORAISA

Special stringency: Melacha she'ein sricha legufa, even though
only miderabanan, is treated MORE strictly than ordinary issurei
derabanan - e.g., one may not ask a non-Jew to do it even for a
mitzva or great need (Mishnah Berurah 278:3).

                                     legufa - assur miderabanan only

                                     behind improved body)


Mishnah Berurah (340:1)              Rules like Ramban/Rivash -
                                     ASSUR MIDORAISA

5. Gramma
Gramma: An indirect act where a melacha occurs as a downstream
consequence of the person's action, not directly. The Tannaim debate
which acts qualify as gramma.

(halacha)               PERMITTED

                        FORBIDDEN

(direct act).

6. Shinui
Shinui: Performing a melacha in an unusual way. Most types of genuine
shinui reduce the melacha from issur doraisa to assur miderabanan.

What Makes Something a Shinui?
Rule                                    Example


Melacha done normally                   Writing with right hand (for right-
everywhere = not a shinui               hander)


Melacha done unusually                  Writing with left hand (for right-
everywhere = shinui                     hander)


Done unusually in one place             Women who spun for the Mishkan
because of unique circumstances
(e.g., spinning directly from goat -
only experts can) = NOT a shinui
for those experts


Done unusually in one place by          Carrying on head in Hutsal - still a
choice (not circumstance) = shinui      shinui
even for locals (batla daatan etsel
kol adam)


Done unusually by one family =          Squeezing pomegranates
always a shinui


Specific Shinui Rulings
Action                                  Status


Carrying heavy items on one's           Assur midoraisa - not a shinui
head                                    (Rambam: only light items =
                                        shinui)
p. 1056. Kavannah U'Maaseh
Carrying light items on one's head     Assur miderabanan - shinui


Writing with weaker hand (right-       Assur miderabanan - shinui
hander writes left)


Erasing with weaker hand               ASSUR MIDORAISA - not a shinui
                                       (Avnei Nezer: erasing works
                                       equally with either hand)


Pressing a button with weaker          ASSUR MIDORAISA - not a shinui
hand


Ambidextrous person writing with       Assur midoraisa - no shinui
either hand


When Is It Permitted to Do a Melacha with a Shinui?
Situation                              Ruling


Kavod ha'brios (human dignity)         PERMITTED - e.g., tearing toilet
                                       paper with elbows, or leaving in
                                       water to tear when flushed


Time of great loss (Magen              Permitted (but Mishnah Berurah
Avraham)                               does not cite this - questionable)


Choleh she'ein bo sakana (issur        PERMITTED with shinui - e.g.,
derabanan only)                        turning on dud shemesh tap


Life-threatening situation (pikuach    Do melacha normally if needed;
nefesh)                                use shinui only if no loss of
                                       effectiveness or speed


Signing name for vital operation       Prefer to sign with weaker hand -
on Shabbos                             reduces to miderabanan
p. 1066. Kavannah U'Maaseh
7. Mekalkel
Mekalkel: Performing a melacha in a purely destructive way - with no
constructive purpose. Such an act is assur miderabanan, not midoraisa.


Action                                   Status


Purely destructive act (tearing          Assur miderabanan - mekalkel
clothing to discard it; destroying an
object to throw it away)


Destructive act in order to              ASSUR MIDORAISA - not
fix/rebuild in the SAME place            mekalkel
(soser al menas livnos - tearing to
sew up, erasing to write over)


Tearing clothing out of anger or         ASSUR MIDORAISA - not
mourning (kria)                          mekalkel (Gemara 105b; halacha
                                         follows this)


Erasing for a constructive purpose       Machlokes: Ritva - miderabanan
other than writing over (e.g., to        (mekalkel). Pri Megadim / Mishnah
remove evidence)                         Berurah - midoraisa. Halacha:
                                         ASSUR MIDORAISA.


Dismantling to rebuild in a              Patur according to Rebbe Yossi;
DIFFERENT place (Rebbe Yossi's           Halacha does not follow this
extra condition)                         strictly




Mekalkel applies to ALL melachos, not only tearing and erasing
(Rashi). Any positive purpose is sufficient to make an act
midoraisa - does not need to be specifically 'al menas litfor /
lichtov' (Biur Halacha 340).
p. 1076. Kavannah U'Maaseh
8. Dvar She'eino Miskayem
Dvar She'eino Miskayem: A melacha whose effect does not last a
sufficient amount of time. Usually assur miderabanan; for certain melachos
(tying, tearing) even permitted.



How Long Must the Effect Last?
Authority                              Standard


Rambam                                 Must last until end of Shabbos to
                                       be considered miskayem


Rashi (implication)                    Must last permanently (or at least
                                       much longer than Shabbos)


Nuances
Rule                                   Example


If it is normal for a substance to     Writing with pencil (normally
produce temporary results, it is       temporary) - chayav. Writing in
NOT considered eino miskayem -         sand - patur (not normal).
still chayav


Effect permanent in itself, made       Writing on flesh - erased by sweat.
temporary by external factor -         Rambam: chayav. Tosefos: patur.
Rambam: not eino miskayem
(chayav). Tosefos: eino miskayem
(patur).


Person intends to undo the             Braiding hair intending to unbraid -
melacha's effect himself - Tosefos:    Tosefos: permitted. Rambam:
eino miskayem (patur / permitted).     chayav.
Rambam: disagrees.
p. 1086. Kavannah U'Maaseh
Knot: not intended to last           Tying a knot intending to untie
permanently - Avnei Nezer: eino      before 24 hours - PERMITTED
miskayem, NOT even assur
miderabanan

1. Foundations - Borrer, Zoreh & Meraked
Defining the Three Melachos
                Method (Rashi          Material (Rashi           Stage in Bread-
 Melacha
                    73a)                    75b)                  Making (Ran)


Borrer         By hand                Removes stones          Middle stage

Zoreh          By wind (thrown        Removes straw           Early stage
               in air)

Meraked        With a sieve           Sifts fine flour        Final stage



The consensus of Poskim: the essential difference is method (first
reason), not material type (second reason).



Is Borrer a Melacha She'ein Sricha L'gufa?
  Authority                   Position                    Practical Consequence


Baal HaMeor       Yes - it is she'ein sricha l'gufa      Still Assur midoraisa since
                  (a negative act of removal)            it was performed in the
                                                         Mishkan

Ramban            No - it is she'sricha l'gufa (a        Chayav because the
                  positive act of cleaning a             Melacha itself is positive in
                  mixture)                               essence

Biur Halacha      Follows the Ramban (based on           This is the operative
                  his ruling re: gozez)                  halachic position
p. 1137. Borrer — Selecting
Is One Chayav for Removing Only Some of the Pesoles?
   Source                                   Ruling


Yerushalmi      Patur unless all pesoles is removed from the mixture (or all
                pesoles from a grogeres-sized portion)

Bavli           Chayav even for removing some of the pesoles

Halacha         Follows the Bavli - Assur midoraisa to remove any pesoles
L'Maaseh        from a mixture



Meshamer - Does It Constitute Borrer?
   Opinion                                  Ruling


Rabbah          Meshamer is included in both Meraked and Borrer (the
                Rambam rules like Rabbah)

Rebbe Zeira     Meshamer is only Meraked, not Borrer (because in Borrer the
                good does not descend)



Bottom Line:
Halacha: One is Chayav for Meshamer under both Meraked and Borrer
(Rambam / SA).



2. The Three Conditions for Permitted
Borrer
To avoid Issur Borrer, all three conditions must be met simultaneously:


   Condition           The Requirement                     If Violated


1. B'Yad - By    Select using one's hand only     Assur midoraisa if kli
Hand             (not a utensil)                  meyuchad; Assur
                                                  miderabanan if other utensil
p. 1147. Borrer — Selecting
   Condition               The Requirement                        If Violated


2. Miyad -            Intend to eat the food right     Assur midoraisa if selecting
Immediately           after selecting                  for later

3. Ochel Mitoch       Remove the food (ochel),         Assur midoraisa to remove
Pesoles - Good        not the pesoles                  pesoles even with hand,
from Bad                                               even immediately



Bottom Line:
All three conditions must be present simultaneously: select with the hand
(b'yad), immediately before eating (miyad), and take the food from the
pesoles (ochel mitoch pesoles).
If any one condition is missing, the act of Borrer is Assur midoraisa.



Why Is B'Yad Permitted?
       Authority                                      Rationale


Shibbolei HaLeket /            Using one's hand is a shinui gamur - a complete
Rashi approach                 deviation from the normal way of doing this
                               Melacha, and therefore totally permitted

Rabbeinu Chananel              Borrer by hand is derech achila - it is part of the
(Rach) / Tosefos               normal eating process, not an act of Melacha

       Scenario                 According to Rashi

                             intent)                       eating now)

5. Taking the Good from the Bad - and Bad
from the Good
Ochel Mitoch Pesoles vs. Pesoles Mitoch Ochel
                         Position on Pesoles from            Position on Ochel
      Authority
                                   Ochel                       from Pesoles


Rambam / Rach /          Always Assur - even by           Permitted if other
Mechaber (SA 319:4)      hand, even for immediate         conditions met
                         use

Tosefos                  One must take whatever is        Permitted if other
                         greater in quantity (may be      conditions met
                         pesoles if it is the majority)

Tur                      Must remove whichever            Permitted if other
                         requires least effort (tircha)   conditions met

Rama (SA 319:4)          Follows Rambam -                 Permitted if other
                         explicitly rejects Tur           conditions met

Mishnah Berurah          Follows Rambam - rejects         Permitted if other
                         Tosefos as well                  conditions met



Bottom Line:
Halacha: It is ALWAYS forbidden to remove pesoles from food - even by
hand, even to eat the food immediately. There is no heter based on
quantity or on effort (tircha). Only ochel from pesoles is permitted.

(a) When There Is No Other Way to Reach the Food

onion)                    ochel from pesoles (Biur Halacha)

6. The Heter of Miyad - Selecting
'Immediately'
Definition of Miyad - Rishonim and Poskim
       Authority                         Definition of 'Immediately'


Ra'avan                     Literally immediately before eating - the strictest
                            opinion

Rabbeinu Chananel           During the course of the meal; extended by
(Rach)                      Acharonim to immediately before the meal

Rabbeinu Yerucham           Any time before the upcoming meal

Rambam (for two types       A few hours before the meal is permitted; only
of food, neither            forbidden if clearly for a later meal
pesoles)

Rav Moshe Feinstein         Includes the preparation time for the meal (if
                            preparation takes one hour, may select anytime in
                            that hour)

Rama / Mishnah              Immediately before the meal; includes the full
Berurah (operative          preparation time needed for that meal
halacha)

           Scenario                                     Ruling

as a separate act

Rambam's Distinction - Genuine Pesoles vs. Two Types of
Food
     Type of Borrer                             Miyad Requirement


Ochel from genuine             Must be immediately before eating (strict definition)
pesoles

Separating two types of        Rambam: permitted even a few hours before next

pesoles)                       immediately before. Rav Elyashiv: lenient based on
                               combination of factors.



Miyad Mamesh - Removing Pesoles at the Very Moment of
Eating
       Authority                                    Ruling


Rosh                       Forbidden to remove pesoles by hand at moment of
                           eating; only the 'tissue at the mouth' heter exists
                           (keeping something out, not removing it)

Ramban                     Lenient - miyad mamesh is permitted (Biur Halacha's
                           reading; disputed by Chazon Ish)

Birchei Yosef /            Strict - forbidden to remove pesoles even at the
Mishnah Berurah            moment of eating
p. 1247. Borrer — Selecting
Bottom Line:
Halacha: One may not remove pesoles by hand immediately before placing
food in the mouth. One may, however, use a tissue or cloth held at the lips
to prevent unwanted material from entering (not a Maaseh Borrer - it is
exclusion, not selection).

                         separating cutlery

                         meal (combination of Tosefos + Rambam's leniency for
                         two types)

Rav Auerbach             Permitted if the table setting genuinely enhances
                         Kavod Shabbos (not merely for convenience)

All agree                Taking one piece of cutlery to wash it = immediate use.
                         Once washed, may place it anywhere.

p. 1308. Tochein — Grinding
               Hilchos Tochein
1. The Definition and Scope of Tochein
Tochein (grinding/cutting) is the Melacha of reducing an object to small
particles. In the Mishkan, herbs were ground into powder for dyes. The
principle: reducing an object to small, usable particles.
SA 321:12: One who cuts vegetables very small is chayav for Tochein.
Rama: forbidden to cut dried figs or carob for elderly people; all this
applies to one who cuts and leaves it - but cutting immediately before
eating is permitted, like the heter of miyad in Borrer.

What Types of Food are Subject to Tochein?
Authority                Position                   Notes


Rambam (Chapter 7,       Chayav for Tochein         Implies: cutting without
Halacha 5)               only when cutting          intent to cook = no
                         vegetables in order to     chiyuv
                         cook them afterwards


Ramach                   Chayav only when (a)       Parallel to his view on
                         cutting in order to cook   bishul
                         AND (b) the vegetable
                         is inedible raw


Tosefos (Shabbos 74b)    Chiyuv only for foods      Later contradiction in
                         that are normally cut      Tosefos resolved:
                         very small (beets as       "beets" = category of
                         prototype)                 normally-cut foods


Rosh                     No chiyuv Tochein          Had a different girsa in
                         applies to cutting food    the Gemara
                         at all


Sefer Yeraim             Assur midoraisa to cut     Does not specify a
p. 1318. Tochein — Grinding
                         any fruit or vegetable     minimum size
                         very small - no
                         restriction on intent or
                         food type


Mechaber (SA 321:12)     Rules like Sefer           Accepted halacha
                         Yeraim - assur
                         midoraisa to cut any
                         fruit or vegetable very
                         small


Magen Avraham            Simple reading: only       Biur Halacha disputes
                         assur to cut food for      this; Chazon Ish
                         someone who cannot         reinterprets MA
                         eat it unless it is cut    differently
                         small


Biur Halacha             Disputes MA - Tochein      Halacha follows Biur
                         is forbidden for           Halacha
                         everyone, even those
                         who could eat the food
                         uncut



How Small Must Food be Cut?
No precise measurement is given by the Rishonim. As a practical guide,
Rav Berkovits suggests: cutting a tomato into 8 pieces is clearly permitted;
more than 8 may enter the prohibition of Tochein. Err on the side of larger
cuts when not eating immediately.

Slicing into Thin Strips - Is it Tochein?
Authority                              Position


Rav Yosef Shalom Elyashiv              STRICT - forbids slicing
                                       carrots/cucumbers into thin slices
                                       (comparable to Tochein)
p. 1328. Tochein — Grinding
Rav Moshe Feinstein                  LENIENT - cutting food into slices is
                                     not a significant enough
                                     improvement to be Tochein


Rav Berkovits                        Follows Rav Feinstein - permitted




Practical Rule: Halacha follows Sefer Yeraim and Biur Halacha. Do not
cut any fruit or vegetable very small unless eating immediately (see
Section 2). No precise shiur, but cut into larger pieces when in doubt.
Thin slicing: permitted per Rav Berkovits/Rav Moshe.
p. 1338. Tochein — Grinding
2. The Heter of Miyad - Cutting Immediately
Before Eating
Just as Borrer is permitted for immediate use (miyad), so too Tochein may
be permitted when done immediately before eating. The rationale: cutting
immediately before eating is considered derech achila - part of the act of
eating, not a Melacha.

The Core Machlokes
Authority                Position                   Notes


Rashba                   Totally permitted to cut   Fundamental heter
                         food very small for
                         immediate eating -
                         derech achila, not
                         Melacha


Shiltei Gibburim         No heter of miyad for      Minority view
                         Tochein - always
                         forbidden to cut very
                         small


Beis Yosef               Essentially agrees with    Chumra l'chatchila
                         Rashba, but rules one
                         should cut slightly
                         larger than normal
                         even for immediate use


Rama (SA 321:12)         Rules like Rashba -        Ashkenaz standard
                         miyad is permitted
                         without the Beis
                         Yosef's chumra


Mishnah Berurah          Many Acharonim follow      L'chatchila follow MB
                         Beis Yosef; ideally cut
                         slightly larger than
p. 1348. Tochein — Grinding
                          normal


Rav Berkovits             B'shaas hadechak
                          (time of need): rely on
                          Rashba/Rama and cut
                          as small as on a
                          weekday




Definition of "immediately": the preparation period immediately before a
meal is included, as long as eating will follow without interruption for other
activities.



Grinding vs. Cutting - Does Miyad Apply to Grinding?
Authority                              Position


Most Poskim                            Miyad applies to grinding as well as
                                       cutting - derech achila covers both


Chazon Ish                             Miyad does NOT apply to
                                       grinding/crushing - crushing is a
                                       significant change to the food's
                                       nature, like Mishkan Tochein.
                                       Forbidden even for immediate use.


Halacha                                Does not follow Chazon Ish. But
                                       ideally: grind in an unusual manner
                                       (shinui) when possible.
p. 1358. Tochein — Grinding
Cutting for Someone Who Cannot Eat the Food
Uncut
Authority                       Position


Most Poskim / Rav Feinstein     Permitted to cut food for someone
                                who cannot eat it uncut (e.g., a child
                                or elderly person), as long as intent
                                is for immediate eating


Chazon Ish                      FORBIDDEN - such a person is
                                categorically like the "zekeinim"
                                case; miyad heter does not apply
                                when the person could not eat the
                                food at all without cutting. Must use
                                a shinui.


Rav Feinstein & Rav Auerbach    Halacha does not follow Chazon Ish.
                                However, ideally be strict for CI if
                                not difficult. Use a shinui when
                                convenient.
p. 1368. Tochein — Grinding

Authority               Position                   Practical Application


Rav Moshe Feinstein     No Tochein -               Halacha follows this
                        banana/avocado do
                        not break into tiny
                        particles; mashing is
                        not comparable to
                        Mishkan grinding


Chazon Ish              Tochein applies -          Stricter position
                        mashing creates a
                        fundamentally changed
                        food form, like grinding
                        dates/figs in the
                        Tosefta

(practical)             m'ikar hadin, ideally be   Ashkenaz
                        strict for Chazon Ish:
                        mash with a spoon or
                        knife handle as shinui




Practical Summary: Cutting immediately before eating = permitted
(follow Rashba/Rama). Ideally cut slightly larger than normal (MB).
Grinding: permitted but use shinui if possible. Mashing
banana/avocado: permitted; ideally use spoon or knife handle as
shinui.
p. 1378. Tochein — Grinding
3. Tochein b'Gidulei Karka - Does Tochein
Apply to Meat, Cheese, and Non-Plant
Foods?
SA 321:9: Permitted to cut cooked or roasted meat very small with a knife.
SA 321:10: Forbidden to grate cheese with a grater.

                         Meat/Cheese

The Mechaber's Two Rulings - Apparent
Contradiction
Sif 9: Permits cutting cooked meat (follows Terumas HaDeshen - meat is
not gidulei karka). Sif 10: Forbids grating cheese with a grater. If cheese is
also not gidulei karka, why is grating forbidden?

Explanation                               Authority


Mechaber's reason for forbidding          Magen Avraham / Tosefes Shabbos
cheese grater is Uvdin d'chol, not
Tochein (since cheese is also not
gidulei karka per SA Sif 9)


Mechaber combines: (a) Uvdin              Tosefes Shabbos / Machsis
d'chol + (b) Shiltei Gibburim's view      HaShekel
that meat/cheese are gidulei karka =
Tochein with kli meyuchad. On Yom
Tov: no Tochein issur, so only Uvdin
d'chol remains - insufficient alone to
forbid.


Gra's view: the grater = Tochein          Gra / Damesek Eliezer
because grating is the normal
derech for cheese - regardless of
gidulei karka. Permitted to cut
cheese with a knife.
p. 1398. Tochein — Grinding
Kli Hameyuchad Lecach - Specialized Cutting
Utensils
A kli hameyuchad lecach is a utensil whose specific purpose is to cut or
grind food (e.g., grater, food processor, mortar and pestle).
Rule                                   Details


Forbidden to use kli meyuchad          Rivash: miyad heter does not apply
lecach even for immediate use          when using such a utensil. Parallel
                                       to Borrer: kli meyuchad = doraisa
                                       even for miyad.


Regular knife = permitted even for     Biur Halacha: knife is derech achila -
cutting very small (for miyad)         part of eating. Not comparable to a
                                       kli meyuchad.


Grater = kli meyuchad lecach           Forbidden to use on Shabbos


Egg slicer / egg cutter                Rav Shlomo-Zalman Auerbach:
                                       NOT a kli meyuchad lecach - merely
                                       a series of blades for slicing.
                                       Permitted to use even on tomatoes.



Cutting Raw Meat for Animals
Rama (321:9): Forbidden to cut raw meat very small for birds - since they
cannot eat it uncut, cutting it constitutes Tochein (making it into food for
the first time). Note: even though meat is not gidulei karka, the exemption
only applies to edible food; raw meat cut for animals is not yet edible.


Practical Summary: Cooked meat - may cut with a knife (no Tochein).
Cheese - do not grate with grater (Tochein / Uvdin d'chol). Any kli
meyuchad lecach is forbidden even for miyad. Egg slicer: permitted.
Raw meat for animals: forbidden.
p. 1408. Tochein — Grinding
4. Tochein Achar Tochein - Re-Grinding
Previously Ground Food
Parallel to Ein bishul achar bishul (no recooking of cooked food), the
Rishonim debate whether once something has been ground, it may be
ground again on Shabbos.

                         grind it again.

                         permitted.

                        tochein. Only crumble

                        tochein achar tochein)




Practical application: crushing medication tablets on Shabbos (where
halachically permitted to consume) - the substances were already ground
before, so Ein tochein achar tochein applies.

p. 1438. Tochein — Grinding
5. Tochein b'Shinui - Grinding in an
Unusual Fashion
SA 321:7: Permitted to crush pepper with the handle of a knife and a bowl.
Normally, crushing with a shinui is assur miderabanan - why is this shinui
totally permitted?



The Concept of Shinui Gamur
Authority                            Position


Sheiltos / Rabbeinu Tam              Gemara (Shabbos 141a) refers to
                                     Yom Tov only - on Shabbos, even
                                     crushing with a shinui is forbidden


Ri / Rosh                            Gemara refers to Shabbos.
                                     Crushing pepper with a knife handle
                                     = totally permitted on Shabbos
                                     because it is a "Shinui gamur" - a
                                     complete/total unusual method


Shibollei HaLeket                    A Shinui gamur is a method so
                                     unusual and inefficient that it is
                                     categorically different from a normal
                                     shinui. It is totally permitted (not
                                     even miderabanan). Same principle
                                     underlies why Borer by hand is
                                     permitted.


Halacha (Gra, Mishnah Berurah)       Ruling like Ri/Rosh: permitted to
                                     crush with knife handle - this is a
                                     Shinui gamur. Use of mortar = Uvdin
                                     d'chol (Taz).
p. 1448. Tochein — Grinding
What Qualifies as a Shinui Gamur?
Example                                Status


Crushing with the handle of a knife    PERMITTED - established as Shinui
                                       gamur in Gemara/SA


Mashing a banana with a spoon          PERMITTED as shinui (Rav Moshe)


Mashing with a fork (normal use)       Rav Ben-Tsion / Rav Ovadia:
                                       permitted. Stricter position: use
                                       spoon/handle instead.


Using a potato masher                  FORBIDDEN - Uvdin d'chol (and
                                       possibly Tochein)


Any other unusual method               Cannot assume it qualifies as Shinui
                                       gamur without a specific ruling from
                                       a qualified Rav
p. 1458. Tochein — Grinding
Tochein of a Previously Cooked Vegetable
Scenario                            Halacha


Mashing a potato that was cooked    FORBIDDEN - Rav Moshe / Rav
before Shabbos (now soft)           Berkovits: cooking softens but does
                                    not constitute Tochein; mashing is
                                    still a new act of Tochein. Must be
                                    thoroughly mashed before Shabbos.


Mashing an over-ripe, very soft     FORBIDDEN - Rav Moshe / Rav
banana                              Berkovits: natural softening does not
                                    exempt from Tochein


Food that was thoroughly mashed     PERMITTED - Ein tochein achar
before Shabbos                      tochein applies (human processing
                                    + not nullified)




Practical Rule: Crush with knife handle = permitted (Shinui gamur).
Spoon for mashing = permitted shinui. Potato masher = forbidden
(Uvdin d'chol). Do not mash cooked potatoes unless already mashed
before Shabbos. Cannot rely on a new shinui method without rabbinic
ruling.
p. 1468. Tochein — Grinding
6. Uvdin d'Chol - Weekday-like Activities
Uvdin d'chol is a Rabbinic prohibition against activities that, while not
technically a Melacha, resemble weekday labor or are incompatible with
the spirit of Shabbos rest.



Source and Status of the Issur
Authority                Position                   Notes


Ramban (Vayikra          There is a positive        Foundational source
23:24)                   Torah mitzvah (based
                         on "Shabbaton") to rest
                         from non-Melacha
                         activities as well.
                         Chazal defined which
                         activities are included.
                         Possibly only an
                         asmachta (Rabbinical
                         with Torah support).


Ritva                    Confirms: basis of
                         resting from non-
                         Melacha activities is
                         from the Torah per
                         Ramban


Rambam / Maggid          Either Torah               Dispute within the
Mishneh                  commanded us to            Rambam's position
                         refrain and Chazal
                         determined specifics,
                         or it is entirely
                         Rabbinical with
                         "tishbos" as an
                         asmachta
p. 1478. Tochein — Grinding
Chasam Sofer              One who opens his
                          store on Shabbos
                          (even without doing
                          Melacha) is called a
                          Shabbos desecrator -
                          confirms the issur has
                          real force




Definition of Uvdin d'Chol
Definition                              Authority


1. The action resembles one of the      Tiferes Yisrael (Kalkeles
39 forbidden Melachos 2. The action     HaShabbos)
could lead to performing a Melacha
3. The action involves excessive
exertion


An action performed in a way similar    Rav Moshe Feinstein
to how one goes about weekday
work - e.g., gathering fruit from a
courtyard into a basket (field-like
activity). Simple home food
preparation is NOT Uvdin d'chol.


Using utensils that store owners use    Rav Shlomo-Zalman Auerbach

Regular household utensils (egg

Two types: (a) could lead to            Rav Pesach Eliyahu Falk

mitzva/great need; (b) involves
excessive exertion only - permitted
for great need or mitzva
p. 1488. Tochein — Grinding
Practical Examples
Activity                                 Status


Gathering fruit from courtyard into a    FORBIDDEN - Uvdin d'chol
large basket                             (resembles field work)


Putting fruit into a small vessel        PERMITTED - not how field work is
                                         done


Using a cheese grater                    FORBIDDEN - Uvdin d'chol (and
                                         possibly Tochein per some opinions)

                                         household utensil, not commercial
                                         equipment

                                         set (Rav Dovid Ribiat)

                                         brush. Minhag: use a designated
                                         Shabbos brush (regular brush may be
                                         Uvdin d'chol / concerns of Gozez).


Grater / food processor                  FORBIDDEN - Uvdin d'chol and/or kli
                                         meyuchad lecach




Uvdin d'chol = Rabbinical prohibition based on "Shabbaton." Activities
that resemble weekday labor, could lead to Melacha, or involve
excessive exertion are forbidden. Commercial-grade or specialized
processing utensils = Uvdin d'chol. Simple home utensils used for
direct food preparation = generally permitted.

p. 1519. Dosh — Threshing
                  Hilchos Dosh
1. The Definition of Dosh
The Melacha of Dosh (threshing) means to extract a substance from that
which encases it. In the Mishkan, herbs were extracted from their casing
for dyeing, and grain was extracted from its casing for bread-making.

Core Definition
Authority               Position                   Key Point


Rashi (Shabbos 73b)     Dosh = "mefarek" -         The casing must be
                        unloading the inner        unusable/inedible; if
                        substance from its         usable, it is not Dosh
                        casing, like unloading a
                        donkey


Tosefos (Shabbos 73b)   Dosh = removing the        Same principle - inner
                        date from its outer peel   extracted from outer


Mishnah Berurah         Distinction: Dosh =        Both Dosh and Borrer
(Sh"Ts 319:15)          dislodging inner matter    can occur
                        from outer casing          simultaneously when
                        (even if some outer        inner is fully separated
                        remains mixed in).         from outer
                        Borrer = separating
                        components in an
                        already-mixed mixture
p. 1529. Dosh — Threshing

melilos) with a shinui on Shabbos:

                         (e.g., fingertips) on
                         Shabbos

                         issur applies even with
                         shinui

                         removing kernel from
                         stalk, since one can
                         eat walnut with peel

                                      doraisa)


Rabbeinu Chananel (Rach)              Assur midoraisa - rubbing by hand is
                                      the Melacha itself

                                      hand = doraisa
p. 1539. Dosh — Threshing
Practical Rule: Do not rub ears of grain or similar actions on Shabbos.
Regarding removing outer peels - see Section 2.




2. Dosh and Peeling Food
Not all peeling constitutes Dosh. The key question is whether the outer
layer is considered a distinct, inedible casing. Several heterim apply.



The Core Distinction: Production Process vs. Home
Peeling

Peeling fruit normally peeled at home   No issur Dosh - this is part of the
before eating (oranges, bananas)        eating process, not production (Rav
                                        Moshe Feinstein, Igros Moshe OC
                                        125)


Peeling done as part of                 Assur - considered Dosh even if
factory/production process (before      done immediately before eating
reaching stores)


Peeling done at home when buying        Permitted (e.g., cracking hard shell
the item with peel attached             of walnut)


Removing outer peel of walnut           FORBIDDEN - this is factory-stage
(green outer layer, removed in          processing (Rav Moshe; Rama)
production)
p. 1549. Dosh — Threshing

Bitul - outer layer is batul to the food    Magen Avraham / R. Akiva Eiger:
                                            peels very closely attached to food
                                            are batul and viewed as part of the
                                            food. Applies to inner garlic/onion
                                            peel.


Outer layer is edible                       Dosh only applies when outer layer
                                            is inedible/unusable. If edible,
                                            removing it = removing one food
                                            layer from another (Magen
                                            Avraham)


Home-use item                               Rav Moshe: if peel is left on until
                                            home use (not removed in factory),
                                            peeling = part of eating, not Dosh
