Important: Borrer Issue Always Applies
Even when there is no issur Dosh in peeling, the issur of Borrer
(separating) applies if one intends to eat the food later rather than
immediately. Always peel immediately before eating.
p. 1569. Dosh — Threshing
3. Dosh b'Gidulei Karka - Does Dosh Apply
to Non-Plant Materials?
The Gemara (Shabbos 75a) records a machlokes Tanaim whether Dosh
applies only to plants or also to animals and other substances.



The Basic Machlokes
Opinion                            Position


Chachamim                          Ein dosh ela b'gidulei karka - Dosh
                                   doraisa applies only to plants. Dosh
                                   on non-plants is assur miderabanan.


Rabbi Yehuda                       Dosh applies even to substances
                                   that are not gidulei karka


Halacha                            Follows Chachamim




Milking a Cow - The Classic Case
The Braissa (Shabbos 95a) states milking a cow is forbidden on Shabbos
as "mefarek," a tolda of Dosh. But a cow is not a plant - how?
Authority              Position                 Explanation


Tosefos                Milking a cow =          Proof from Gemara
                       doraisa only per Rabbi   that milking with shinui
                       Yehuda; per              is needed for pain-
                       Chachamim only           relief - implies without
                       miderabanan              shinui = doraisa
p. 1579. Dosh — Threshing
Rambam           Milking a cow = assur    Seemingly contradicts
                 doraisa                  Ein dosh ela b'gidulei
                                          karka


Maggid Mishneh   Rambam: cow is           Fish: only miderabanan
                 considered gidulei       per Rambam
                 karka because it is
                 nourished by plants.
                 Fish are not (not
                 nourished by plants).


Rav Avraham b.   Ein dosh ela b'gidulei
Rambam           karka applies only to
                 the Av Melacha.
                 Mefarek (the tolda)
                 applies even to non-
                 gidulei karka - so
                 milking = doraisa
                 regardless


Rashba / Rach    Milking = doraisa (cow
                 is gidulei karka). Rav
                 Hai Gaon: only
                 miderabanan.
p. 1589. Dosh — Threshing
The Eglei Tal's Rules
Rule                                      Application


If outer casing is gidulei karka, Dosh    E.g., squeezing water out of cotton
applies - even if inner substance is      (for the water) = Dosh doraisa -
not                                       cotton is gidulei karka


If outer casing is NOT gidulei karka,     E.g., squeezing oil out of fish for the
no Dosh doraisa - even if inner           oil = not doraisa - fish is not gidulei
substance is gidulei karka                karka


Dosh applies to materials found
within the karka itself, not only
things that grow from it


Dosh does NOT apply to something          If it did, every act of kotser would
attached to the ground                    also be Dosh




Practical Rule: It is assur miderabanan to milk a cow on Shabbos (at
minimum), and most Poskim hold it is assur midoraisa. L'maaseh it is
fully forbidden.
p. 1599. Dosh — Threshing
4. Sechita b'Peiros - Squeezing Fruit (Part 1)
Squeezing liquid from fruit is a form of Dosh (or a tolda thereof). There are
three categories of fruit with different levels of issur.



Three Categories of Fruit

Commonly squeezed        Olives, grapes               ASSUR MIDORAISA to
for juice                                             squeeze

for juice                pomegranates (and            MIDERABANAN to
                         nowadays, most fruit)        squeeze


Never squeezed for       Possibly gooseberries,       PERMITTED to
juice                    cucumbers                    squeeze


Note: Nowadays, almost all fruit are sometimes squeezed. Therefore, the
miderabanan category applies broadly.

                          permitted to squeeze

                          is to improve the taste
                          of the fruit itself.

Practical Summary: Squeezing grapes or olives = assur doraisa.
Squeezing most modern fruit = assur miderabanan. Squeezing fruit

squeeze directly onto food where possible - see Section 5.

Summary - Squeezing Wet Material
Squeezing material soaked in water = assur (Melabein). If also
intending to collect the water = also assur doraisa (Dosh). Squeezing
material with colored liquid = assur (Melabein per MB); if intending to
collect = doraisa. Do not wipe with very wet sponge without a handle.

p. 17610. Melabein — Laundering
                            Melabein


1. Foundations - The Melacha of Melabein
Melabein (whitening/laundering) in the Mishkan involved cleansing the
wool shorn from animals. The core question debated by the Rishonim is
whether Melabein is limited to washing with water or extends to other
forms of cleaning.



The Core Question: Can There Be Melabein Without Water?
Authority        Position                              Notes


Rashi (Shabbos   Melabein mid'oraisa requires water    BUT: Rashi also
141a)            - scraping dirt from the outside of   implies (Shabbos
                 clothing is only derabanan            146b) that shaking
                                                       dust from a Tallis is
                                                       chayav chataas - an
                                                       apparent
                                                       contradiction


Shaar HaTzion    Resolves the contradiction:           If a stain remains
(302:41)         Melabein without water is             after cleaning without
                 mid'oraisa only when the dirt is      water, no issur
                 completely removed                    doraisa. Rubbing a
                                                       kerchief (already
                                                       clean) = only
                                                       derabanan even per
                                                       Rashi


Rach & Tosefos   No Melabein without water - period    The shaking case in
(Shabbos 177a)                                         the Gemara involved
                                                       dew; the water in the
                                                       dew causes the
p. 17710. Melabein — Laundering
                                                           cleaning


Mechaber (SA      Rules like Rach/Tosefos - no             Lenient position
302:1)            Melabein without water


Rama (SA          Cites Rashi - one should be strict       Ashkenazic practice
302:1)                                                     follows Rama


Rav Ovadia        Sefardim may be lenient and shake        Follows Mechaber's
Yosef             dust off clothing even if makpid         ruling




Bottom Line: Mechaber rules leniently (no Melabein without water). Rama
rules strictly. Ashkenazim follow Rama. Sefardim may follow Mechaber.




2. Cleaning Without Water - Rubbing Clothing
Rubbing Clothing to Soften vs. to Whiten
The Gemara (Shabbos 140a) distinguishes between rubbing clothing to
soften it (permitted) and rubbing to whiten it (forbidden). Intent is the
determining factor for regular clothing - but for certain items (kerchiefs,
linen), intent is presumed to be whitening.


                  Rambam /              Raavad /
Item                                                         Rama / MB
                  Mechaber              Ramban


Regular (non-     Permitted -           Permitted            Permitted unless
linen) clothing   presumed intent is                         clearly intending to
                  to soften                                  whiten (MB
                                                             302:24)


Kerchief          Forbidden -           Permitted if not     Forbidden
(mitpachas)       presumed intent is    intending to         (Mechaber rules
                  to whiten/shine       whiten               like Rambam)
p. 17810. Melabein — Laundering
Linen clothing     -                       -                   Forbidden - same
(not                                                           status as kerchief
undergarment)                                                  (Shibbolei
                                                               HaLeket, cited by
                                                               Rama; MB 302:25)


Linen              -                       -                   Permitted - nobody
undergarment                                                   sees it, so intent is
                                                               presumed to be
                                                               softening, not
                                                               whitening (MB)




Practical Rule: Do not rub a kerchief or any visible linen garment.
Rubbing non-linen clothing to soften it is permitted, but forbidden if you
clearly intend to whiten it. Linen undergarments may be rubbed.



3. Shaking Dust or Dew from Clothing
The Gemara's Conditions: New, Black, and Makpid
The Gemara forbids shaking a new, black Tallis of dew/dust only when the
person is makpid (particular) about not wearing it with that dirt. The Biur
Halacha (302, Dh: Aleha) clarifies that 'makpid' is the essential factor;
'new' and 'black' are merely indicators that a person tends to be makpid on
such a Tallis.
Authority              Explanation of Why These Conditions Matter


Rambam                 The issur is not Melabein at all - it is Makeh B'patish
(Shabbos               (completing an object). Removing leftover production
10:16,18)              material to make the Tallis wearable constitutes the final
                       act of completing it - forbidden only if makpid


Rashba (cited by       Follows Rach: the person shakes dew, and cleaning is a
Maggid Mishneh)        side effect. If makpid, we assume he wants the cleaning -
                       forbidden. If not makpid (would wear it as-is), cleaning is
                       eino miskavein - permitted
p. 17910. Melabein — Laundering
Biur Halacha           New and black are not absolute conditions - they are
(302:2)                predictors of makpid. A person who is known to be
                       makpid on an old or white Tallis is also forbidden to shake
                       it


Practical Halacha - Shaking Clothing
Scenario                              Halacha L'Maaseh


Shaking dust from new black           FORBIDDEN mid'oraisa per Rashi;
Tallis (makpid)                       Rama rules strictly


Shaking dust when NOT makpid          PERMITTED - Rashba: cleaning is eino
(would wear it dirty)                 miskavein


Shaking dust on Shabbos               FORBIDDEN - since Shabbos requires
(Ashkenazim generally)                best dress, person is presumed makpid
                                      (Poskim)


Shaking dust from old garment         Biur Halacha: strict; permits only with
                                      shinui (back of hand)

p. 18010. Melabein — Laundering
4. Cleaning with Water
The Gemara (Zevachim 94a) rules: 'Shriyuso zehu kibuso' - for fabric
material, soaking IS laundering. Even placing a small amount of water on
fabric without scrubbing constitutes Melabein mid'oraisa. However, several
Gemaras appear to contradict this, and the Rishonim offer two main
resolutions.

              2nd opinion)   way of cleaning.            (not derech kibbus).

                             dirties (derech lichluch)   on children's soiled

Key Rule: Placing water on any stain or dirt = forbidden mid'oraisa.
Wetting clean fabric = dispute; MB rules strictly. Leather = more lenient
(wetting permitted; scrubbing forbidden).




5. Drying Wet Clothes and the Gezeiros Against
Squeezing
Drying Wet Clothes with Heat
The Mordechai rules that drying wet clothing by a fire constitutes Melabein
(and also Bishul) because it assists the cleaning process. The Biur
Halacha (302) extends this to drying in the sun as well.

p. 18711. Losh — Kneading
                               Losh


Definition of Losh
Losh (kneading): Combining tiny particles into a solid or semi-solid mass
by means of a liquid. Many Poskim include adding and mixing liquid into a
thick sauce or pasty substance. In the Mishkan: ground herbs mixed with
water into thick paste.
Key Terms
Term                                 Definition


Bar Gibul                            Two substances that fuse well
                                     through kneading. Classic
                                     example: flour and water.


Lav Bar Gibul                        Two substances that do NOT fuse
                                     well. Classic example: ash and
                                     water.


Blilah Avah                          Thick mixture (e.g., stiff dough,
                                     thick paste)


Blilah Racah                         Loose mixture (e.g., thin batter,
                                     runny consistency)


Shinui Seder                         Reversing the normal order in
                                     which ingredients are combined


Shinui Gibul                         Mixing in an unusual way (e.g.,
                                     with a finger, criss-cross, small
                                     amounts at a time)
p. 18811. Losh — Kneading
1. Bar Gibul - When Does Losh Begin?
Machlokes Tanaim: At what point does the issur doraisa of losh apply?

                        liquid is placed into    HaTerumah rule like
                        the dry substance -      Rebbe
                        before any stirring

Yehuda (halacha)        actively kneads the      Mechaber rule like
                        combination. Placing     RYbY
                        liquid = assur
                        miderabanan only.

Rebbe as 'yesh omrim.' Pri Megadim: Even Rebbe Yosi Bar Yehuda
holds that placing water into a bar gibul is assur miderabanan.
p. 18911. Losh — Kneading

                      gibul




Yesh Losh Achar Losh: It is assur midoraisa to knead a mixture
that has already been kneaded. One cannot 're-knead' a pre-made
dough and assume it is permitted (Biur Halacha, based on
Yerushalmi).
p. 19011. Losh — Kneading

p. 19712. Me'abed — Tanning
                             Me'abed

1. Foundations
What Is Me'abed?
Me'abed (tanning) involves preserving and hardening animal hides. It was
required in the Mishkan to prepare the hides used as coverings. The
melacha consists of applying salt or brine to raw hides, drawing out
moisture and causing them to dry and harden.



Does Me'abed Apply to Food? - The Core Machlokes Rishonim
Authority         Position                              Notes


Rach (Rabbeinu    No issur of Me'abed with food -       Rules like Rava - Ein
Chananel)         totally permitted to salt even        ibud b'ochlin
                  heavily


Rambam            No issur of Me'abed with food - all   Agrees with Rach on
(Shabbos          food-salt prohibitions stem from      this fundamental point
22:10)            bishul


Rashi & Tosefos   Issur derabanan of Me'abed            Rules that heavily
(Shabbos 75b)     applies to food                       salting food resembles
                                                        tanning


Rava (Shabbos     Ein ibud b'ochlin - no Me'abed        Even Rabbah bar Huna
75b)              with food at all                      agrees: light salting for
                                                        eating = permitted


Rabbah bar        Heavily salting meat = Me'abed        Rav Ashi: he agrees
Huna (Shabbos     mid'oraisa                            light salting to eat is not
75b)                                                    Me'abed
p. 19812. Me'abed — Tanning
Bottom Line: The Rach and Rambam permit salting food freely. Rashi and
Tosefos hold there is an issur derabanan. The Mechaber rules like
Rashi/Tosefos for most cases (see below).



2. Salt Water - Hilmi
The Issur to Make Salt Water
Chazal forbade making hilmi (a large concentration of salt water) on
Shabbos. The Mechaber (SA 321:2) follows Rashi that this resembles the
tanning process, where a brine solution was prepared to soak hides.


Scenario                                 Halacha L'Maaseh


Large amount of salt water               FORBIDDEN - resembles Me'abed
                                         (Rashi) / tikunim of bishul (Rambam)


Small amount of salt water (for          PERMITTED - small amounts were
immediate use)                           never made in tanning process


Very strong salt water - 2/3 salt, 1/3   FORBIDDEN - resembles muryas
water (even small amount)                (fish pickling brine) per SA 321:2


Adding oil before adding salt to small   PERMITTED - oil prevents
amount of water                          resemblance to Me'abed (MB 321:10-
                                         11)


Adding oil after salt water has          FORBIDDEN - oil only helps if added
already been made                        before the salt (MB)


Making salt water for a later meal       PERMITTED per Mishnah Berurah;
(small amount)                           Magen Avraham is strict


Making large salt water to put into a    Tosefes Shabbos: permitted;
cooked dish                              Mishnah Berurah: strict


The Ran's Limitation on Small Amounts
p. 19912. Me'abed — Tanning
Authority               Position


Ran (plain reading)     Permitted to make as much salt water as needed for one
                        meal; forbidden to make more for a later meal


Magen Avraham           Interprets Ran more strictly: forbidden to make any
                        amount of salt water if intent is for a later meal - even if
                        small


Mishnah Berurah         Rejects Magen Avraham - permits a small amount of salt
(321:10)                water even for a later meal

Since the issur is because salting resembles pickling, if the item is not
normally pickled in that form, it is permitted.

4. Salting Eggs and Cooked Meat
Is There an Issur at All?
The Rambam holds there is no issur to salt eggs or cooked meat for any
duration, since pickling does not apply to them. Rashi holds there can be a
Me'abed-type issur if they are left in salt long enough to harden. The
Mechaber (SA 321:5) is strict like Rashi.



How Long Is 'Too Long'?
Authority             Position


Taz and Magen         Forbidden if intent is to eat at a later meal - even later in
Avraham               the same day


Mishnah Berurah       Lenient - only forbidden if intent is to keep until after
(321:21)              Shabbos; permits salting for a later meal on the same day


Halacha L'Maaseh      Follow Mishnah Berurah - salting eggs/cooked meat for
                      any Shabbos meal is permitted




Practical Rule: One may salt eggs or cooked meat for any Shabbos meal.
Salting them to keep until after Shabbos is forbidden.
p. 20212. Me'abed — Tanning

not yet third day

                                                          Authority He
Topic                    Mechaber's Approach
                                                          Follows


Salt water (hilmi)       Forbidden because it resembles   Rashi and Tosefos
                         Me'abed

                         pickling - which resembles
                         bishul

meat/eggs to leave       Rashi's view that hardening      explanation)
                         effect constitutes Me'abed
p. 20312. Me'abed — Tanning
The Pri Megadim (321:3,5) explains the Mechaber's mixed rulings: for salt
water, most Rishonim agree with Rashi so he followed Rashi. For
vegetables, the Rambam's reason (resemblance to pickling) is more
readily understandable than Rashi's (a small amount of salt causing
Me'abed hardening), so he followed the Rambam there.

p. 20513. Muktza
                   Hilchos Muktza

1. Foundations


Status of the Prohibition
Muktza is an issur miderabanan. Rashi (Pesachim 47b) appeared to hold it has a
Torah source, but Tosefos (Pesachim 30a) definitively ruled otherwise. The
halacha follows Tosefos.


The Core Machlokes: Rebbe Yehuda vs. Rebbe Shimon

Position                 View on Muktza

Rebbe Yehuda             Strict - any item set aside for a specific, forbidden
                         purpose may not be moved or used for another
                         purpose.

Rebbe Shimon             Lenient - if an item has possible alternative uses, the
                         person never fully 'sets it aside' mentally and it is
                         not Muktza. The issur exists but is far more limited.



Which Posek Follows Which Opinion?

Authority           Shabbos                       Yom Tov

Rif / Rambam /      Rebbe Shimon (lenient)        Rebbe Yehuda (strict)
Mechaber (SA)

Rabbeinu Tam /      Rebbe Shimon for regular      Same as Shabbos
Rama                Muktza; Rebbe Yehuda
                    for Nolad
p. 20613. Muktza
Authority             Shabbos                          Yom Tov

Rach / Mishnah        Rebbe Shimon (lenient)           Rebbe Shimon except for
Berurah                                                Nolad

             The halacha follows the Mishnah Berurah (=Rach): Rebbe Shimon
 Halacha
             always, except Nolad on Yom Tov.



Nolad - Something That Came into Existence on Shabbos
Nolad is a sub-category of Muktza for items that did not exist (or were in a totally
different state) before Shabbos. Examples:
   • An egg laid on Shabbos - Muktza according to all opinions.
   • Seeds that were in fruit at the onset of Shabbos and fell out on Shabbos -
       Muktza according to Rebbe Yehuda; Rebbe Shimon is lenient on Shabbos.
   • Condensation from an air conditioner - Nolad according to all opinions;
       assur to move.



2. The Five Categories of Muktza


Category 1: Muktza Machmas Gufa
Items with no conceivable Shabbos use - they are inherently set aside.
   • Examples: Stones, raw money, dirt.
   • For food: requires (a) dechiya beyadayim - an active act that made it
       inedible, AND (b) lo chazi - it is totally inedible. E.g., figs placed on a roof
       to dry (grogeres, tzimukim).
   • For non-food items (e.g., stones): the two conditions above are not
       required.
   • Rambam: only condition for food is that it is totally inedible - no
       requirement of dechiya beyadayim. Mechaber rules like Rashi/Tosefos:
       both conditions required for food.
p. 20713. Muktza
Category 2: Muktza Machmas Chisaron Kis
Items the person is careful to use only for their designated purpose, never to use
them casually, and keeps in a set place - out of fear of financial loss.
   • Examples: Expensive tools, a mohel's scalpel, writing instruments
      (lechatchila - Rav Berkovits).
   • A wallet: The Elyah Rabbah rules it is generally Kli shemelachto l'issur, not
      Muktza machmas chisaron kis, since most people also keep non-Muktza
      items in their wallet.
   • A bed designated for money: If money is on it during Bein hashmashos,
      the bed becomes a bassis (see Section 4).
   • Wall clocks/paintings: Chazon Ish rules they are Muktza machmas
      chisaron kis. Rav Moshe Feinstein disagrees - they stay in place for
      function/decoration, not fear of damage.
   • Pesach cutlery: Rav Auerbach rules it is NOT Muktza machmas chisaron kis
      - the reason the person is careful with it is not one of the reasons
      recognized by Chazal.

Category 3: Muktza Machmas Issur
Items that were forbidden to use as Shabbos began, where there was also
dechiya beyadayim (an active act that caused the forbidden state).
   • Classic example: A candle lit before Shabbos. The act of lighting = dechiya
      beyadayim; it is forbidden to move while lit. After it goes out, Rebbe Meir
      holds it remains Muktza. Rebbe Shimon permits - he expected it to go out
      (yoshev u'metsapeh).
   • Halacha follows Rebbe Meir (strict) re: Muktza machmas issur. The
      Mechaber rules a lit candle's wax remains Muktza after it goes out.
   • Animal carcass that died on Shabbos: NOT Muktza machmas issur - there
      was no dechiya beyadayim; the person did nothing to cause the issur.
      Permitted to feed to one's animals (Mechaber, SA 324:7).
   • Vegetable cut by a non-Jew on Shabbos: IS Muktza machmas issur - the
      Beis Yosef explains that failing to pick it before Shabbos is itself treated as
      dechiya beyadayim (a minor act to do; not doing it shows intent).



             Muktza machmas issur requires dechiya beyadayim - an active act
Key Rule     (or its near-equivalent) that put the object into a forbidden state
             as Shabbos began.
p. 20813. Muktza
Category 4: Kli Shemelachto L'issur
A utensil whose primary function is forbidden on Shabbos, but which has
possible permitted uses. This is a more lenient category of Muktza - it may be
moved in two situations:

Permitted Reason to       Examples
Move

L'sorech gufo - to use    Using a hammer to crack open nuts; using a knife for
the kli itself for a      food.
permitted purpose

L'sorech mekomo - the     Moving a hammer off the couch to sit down.
kli is in the way and
you need the space

   • If neither condition applies - do not move.
   • Kli shemelachto l'issur with NO possible permitted use at all: Baal HaMeor
       rules it is Muktza machmas gufa. Rashba rules it remains Kli shemelachto
       l'issur. Rav Moshe and Rav Berkovits rule leniently like the Rashba.
       Examples: umbrellas, thermometers, telephones.


Category 5: Kli Shemelachto L'heter
A utensil whose primary function is permitted on Shabbos. It may be moved for
any purpose, including l'tsorech gufo or even without any need at all. Examples:
plates, cups, books.



3. Selected Practical Cases

Balls and Toys

Authority                Ruling

Mechaber (SA             Balls are Muktza machmas gufa - no valid kli function.
308:45)
p. 20913. Muktza
Authority               Ruling

Rav Elyashiv, Rav       Balls today are manufactured for play; Mechaber
Auerbach, Rav           would be lenient.
Wosner

Rav Ovadia Yosef,       Mechaber is strict even today. A child may rely on the
Rav Abba Shaul          Rama.

Rama (and Minhag)       Lenient - balls (and toys that do no Melacha) are not
                        Muktza.

Mishnah Berurah         Appears lenient. Minhag is to be lenient.

Pets and Animals
   • All non-domesticated animals: Muktza according to everyone.
   • Pets: Machlokes Rishonim (Rosh is strict; Maharich Ohr Zaruah is lenient).
      Consensus among Poskim: even pets are Muktza.
   • Fish tank: Rav Auerbach permits moving the tank (not the fish) - the tank
      serves a decorative function, not the fish alone, so it is not a bassis.

Flames and Electric Elements
   • A lit candle: Muktza - it is a bassis to the flame, which is Muktza.
   • Electric appliance with a heating element (lamp, hot plate, electric
      blanket): Machlokes. Rav Elyashiv: Muktza machmas gufa. Rav Moshe
      Feinstein, Rav Berkovits: Not Muktza machmas gufa - but it is Kli
      shemelachto l'issur.
   • Practical implication: May move such appliances l'sorech gufo or l'sorech
      mekomo only.



Keilim That Get Used Up
   • Candles, soap, erasers, pencils: Mor U'ketsiah rules they lack shem kli and
     are Muktza. Mishnah Berurah rules they are not Muktza (but may be Kli
     shemelachto l'issur).
   • Rav Berkovits: Lechatchila be strict for the Mor U'ketsiah with pencils,
     soap, and erasers.
p. 21013. Muktza
4. Bassis L'Dvar Issur


If Muktza rests intentionally on a non-Muktza object as Bein hashmashos begins,
the supporting object (bassis) itself becomes Muktza - with the same severity as
the Muktza placed upon it. It remains Muktza even if the Muktza item is removed
during Shabbos.

                            Bassis?

                                          chashuv and move together.



Bassis L'Dvar Heter V'Issur - Mixed Contents
If non-Muktza items of greater importance are also on the object during Bein
hashmashos, the object does NOT become Muktza.
   • 'Greater importance' is measured by necessity for Shabbos - not financial
       value.
   • Example: Challos and candlesticks on the Shabbos table. Since the challos
       are more needed, the table is not a bassis.
   • Money in a drawer that also has clothing needed for Shabbos: drawer
       does not become Muktza.

Gamru Bidei Adam - Inevitable Completion
If an item was in an unusable state as Shabbos began, but it was certain (not just
possible) that it would become usable on Shabbos, it is not Muktza when it
becomes usable.

6. Bittul Kli Miheichano


It is forbidden to actively make a kli Muktza on Shabbos by placing Muktza into it
or on it - this is called bittul kli miheichano (nullifying a utensil from its
[permitted] use).


Rules
   • Forbidden even for a short period - unless there is significant financial loss
        (Mishnah Berurah).
   • Permitted for a very short time, if the Muktza can be immediately shaken
        off.
   • Permitted for the whole Shabbos in a case of tzaar baalei chaim (animal
        suffering).
   • Permitted to place Kli shemelachto l'issur on a permitted item (it is still
        movable in certain situations). Forbidden to place Muktza machmas gufa
        on it.

Practical Cases

Case                              Ruling

Placing bucket under air          FORBIDDEN - bittul kli miheichano. Permitted
conditioner drip (water =         only if a more chashuv non-Muktza item is also
Nolad)                            in the bucket.

Making clothing very dirty        FORBIDDEN - renders the garment Muktza.
so it cannot be worn
p. 21513. Muktza
Case                           Ruling

Putting garbage into a         PERMITTED - this is the bin's primary use.
garbage bin

Putting garbage into plastic   PERMITTED - commonly used this way.
bags / plates

Placing pillows under glass    PERMITTED - significant financial loss.
keilim (to prevent breakage)

p. 21714. Refuah — Medical Treatment
           Hilchos Refuah on Shabbos

1. The Five Categories of People

Chazal forbade refuah (medical treatment) on Shabbos out of concern that a
person would grind herbs to make medicine - transgressing the Melacha of
Tochein. The scope of this gezeira depends on the person's level of illness.


Category           Definition                    Refuah Status on Shabbos

1. Totally         No illness whatsoever.        May consume Maachal briyim
healthy person                                   freely. Issur refuah on non-
                                                 Maachal-briyim items if intent
                                                 is health (MA; MB).

2. Baal            Somewhat unwell;              May consume Maachal briyim.
meichush           walking around.               Forbidden to take non-
                                                 Maachal-briyim items for
                                                 refuah; Machlokes if for eating
                                                 only (Elyah Rabbah strict).

3. Choleh          Severely ill throughout       May take medicine (minhag);
she'ein boh        body; not life-               may ask non-Jew to do
sakana             threatening. Bed-ridden       Melacha doraisa; Jew may do
                   OR whole body feels           Issur derabanan with shinui
                   weak.                         (Ramban/MB).

4. Sakanas eiver   Limb at risk of being lost;   All Issurei derabanan permitted
                   not life-threatening.         (Ran, Ramban).

5. Choleh          Life-threatening              All Issurei doraisa permitted
she'yesh boh       situation.                    and obligatory; Shabbos is
sakana                                           docheh.
p. 21814. Refuah — Medical Treatment
             Chazal did not forbid refuah for animals - the Rif explains that a
  Why        person does not panic about an animal's illness the same way he
Animals?     panics about his own, so the concern of grinding herbs does not
             apply.



2. Maachal Briyim - Food of Healthy People

Maachal briyim refers to food and drink consumed by healthy people, even if
some eat it primarily for health. It is the key concept that separates permitted
from forbidden consumption for Baalei Meichush.


Rules by Person Type

                                               Auerbach: MA applies to all.

                          specific area. Totally healthy person - permitted.

                          (Maachal briyim). Most Poskim dispute this.

Sefardim (Mechaber)       Permitted - healthy person may consume non-
                          Maachal-briyim for any reason.



3. Scope of the Gezeira & Non-Medication Treatments

The gezeira only applies to treatments where there is a concern the person will
grind herbs (i.e., treatments that could be replaced by medication). Treatments
for which no medication could be used are not within the gezeira - but may still
be forbidden due to Uvdin d'chol.


Treatment                        Status

Hot cup on stomach for pain      Permitted - no herb-grinding concern;
                                 permitted even for Baal meichush.

Back exercises for back pain     Forbidden - pain could theoretically be treated
                                 with medication, so any form of refuah is
                                 included in the gezeira (Orchos Shabbos).

Vigorous self-massage /          Forbidden if for health (Rambam/Biur
rubbing hard                     Halacha). Permitted for pleasure with a shinui
                                 (SA 327:2).

Rubbing with feet on saliva      Permitted - not done for health, not
                                 Memarayach (Magen Avraham).

Bathing in healing waters        Forbidden - either Uvdin d'chol or healing
(Diomsis-type)                   waters.

Sunbathing for health            Forbidden (Chelkas Yaakov). Also possible

Treatment                      Status

                               Tzovaya if tanning is intended (Minchas
                               Yitzchak). Rav Fisher and Shemiras Shabbos
                               K'Hilchasa: no Tzovaya issue.

Physiotherapy / exercises      Forbidden today even without sweating - the
                               modern equivalent is done for health (Orchos
                               Shabbos), which brings it into the gezeira.

Mouthwash                      Permitted - removes bad breath only, not the
                               source of bad breath (Eglei Tal distinction).

6. Choleh She'yesh Boh Sakana - Pikuach Nefesh


                 It is not only permitted but obligatory to break Shabbos to save
Fundamental
                 a life. One who acts with alacrity is praiseworthy (Rambam).
    Rule
                 One who is unnecessarily hesitant is to be rebuked.


Hutra or Dechuya - Nature of the Heter
Authority                 Position

Maharam                   Shabbos is Hutra - as if no Issur is being committed at
MiRottenburg /            all. Comparable to Yom Tov Melacha for food.
Avnei Nezer (reading
of Rambam)

Rashba, Ran, simple       Shabbos is Dechuya - the Issur is present but
reading of Rambam         overridden.
(Halacha 1)

Mishnah Berurah           Appears to hold Dechuya.


Defining 'Danger' - When Do We Act?
Scenario                         Ruling

Safek (doubt) whether life is    Break Shabbos - safek nefashos lehakel.
at risk

Sfek sfeika (double doubt)       Break Shabbos.

Will extend life only briefly    Break Shabbos (Chai bahem principle).

Person sentenced to death        Biur Halacha: forbidden to break Shabbos for
by Beis Din                      him.

Not in danger today but          Break Shabbos to prevent the future danger
danger in future                 (SA 328:11; MB).
p. 22614. Refuah — Medical Treatment
Scenario                       Ruling

Certain that not doing         Wait until after Shabbos.
Melacha will NOT endanger


What Melachos are Permitted?
Authority             Scope

Rambam / Ramban /     Permitted to do any Melacha normally done in the
Mechaber              week for the Choleh - even non-life-saving needs.

Rashi and many        Only Melacha directly connected to saving the life.
Rishonim

Biur Halacha          Non-life-saving Melachos should be done by a non-
                      Jew; Melachos strengthening the Choleh where
                      weakness could be dangerous - permitted by a Jew.


By Whom Should the Melacha Be Done?
Authority             Ruling

Rambam / Mechaber     A Jew (adult man) should do the Melacha - not non-
                      Jew, woman, or child. (Concern about misimpression
                      that it is forbidden for Jews to do Melacha for pikuach
                      nefesh.)

Tosefos / Rama        If there is no concern that the non-Jew will be lax:
                      better that he do it. This is the minhag.

Taz                   A Jew will act with greater urgency - better that he do
                      the Melacha.


Doing Melacha with a Shinui
Authority             Ruling

Ramban                In all cases of pikuach nefesh, if it can be done with a
                      shinui without dangerous delay - must do shinui.
p. 22714. Refuah — Medical Treatment
Authority                Ruling

Rambam / Mechaber        The shinui requirement is limited to a Yoledes
                         (childbirth). Other cases: no shinui required.

Rama                     Rules like Ramban - shinui where possible in all
                         pikuach nefesh cases.


Miscellaneous Pikuach Nefesh Rules
   • Doing Melacha to allay the Choleh's fear: Permitted (Ramban, Tosefos) -
       fear itself is dangerous.
   • Husband accompanying wife in labor to hospital: Permitted if she is afraid
       to go alone (Rav Moshe).
   • Intending for additional Melacha while saving a life (e.g., catching fish
       while saving baby): Machlokes Rishonim. MB appears strict.
   • Marbeh b'shiurim: Forbidden - do not perform Melacha on a larger
       quantity than necessary. Better to do one act on a larger amount than two
       acts on a smaller amount.



7. Doctors, Patients & Who Decides


Scenario                           Ruling

Choleh says 'I need to eat';       Feed the Choleh - everyone agrees.
one doctor says no

Choleh says 'I don't need';        Feed the Choleh - everyone agrees.
one doctor says he does

Choleh says 'I need'; two          Rav Yannai: Follow doctors (don't feed). Mar
doctors say he doesn't             Bar Rav Ashi, Rach, Rambam, Mechaber: Feed
                                   the Choleh.

Two doctors say he needs to        Ramban, Rosh, Mechaber: Feed him - safek
eat; majority say he doesn't       nefashos lehakel. Rashi, Rambam: Follow
                                   majority.

on each side                   Magen Avraham).

Non-doctor onlooker says it    Permitted to break Shabbos if a Jew; if no Jew
is life-threatening            expert, ask non-Jew to do Melacha (Mishnah
                               Berurah).

                               self-assessment.

disagrees



8. Yoledes - Woman in Labor

A Yoledes (woman in labor) has the halachic status of Choleh she'yesh boh
sakana from a certain point in labor.


When Does Pikuach Nefesh Status Begin?
Stage of Labor                 Status

Yoshev al hamishbar (sits in   Permitted to do Melachos - Abaye; Rif rules
labor position)                like this.

Blood flows                    Permitted - Rav Huna (lenient version).

Needs friends to help her      Permitted - Rav Huna (another version).
walk

Crying out in pain (before     Rambam: Permitted to light a candle at this
above stages)                  point, even before the full onset.

Any of the above -             SA rules like Ramban: permitted at whichever
whichever comes first          stage occurs first.
p. 22914. Refuah — Medical Treatment
Stage of Labor                  Status

Before any stage, if delay      Permitted; certainly permitted to travel to
risks danger                    hospital early.


Status After Birth
Period                       Status

Days 1–3 after birth         Choleh she'yesh boh sakana - even if she says she
                             doesn't need it.

Days 3–7                     Choleh she'yesh boh sakana if she says she needs
                             it. If she says she doesn't - forbidden.

Days 7–30                    Choleh she'ein boh sakana - non-Jew should do
                             any needed Melachos.

After 30 days                Healthy; normal halachos apply.

Counting the 3 days          MB: count m'eis l'eis (72 hours) - lenient for safek
                             nefashos lehakel.



9. Saving a Non-Jew & Limiting Chillul Shabbos


Saving a Non-Jew on Shabbos
Scenario                     Ruling

Breaking Shabbos Issurei     Forbidden (Rambam).
doraisa to save non-Jew
(no enmity concern)

Issurei derabanan if         Permitted - most Poskim.
enmity (eivah) concern

Issurei doraisa if enmity    Tzitz Eliezer: Permitted if the Melacha is she'ein
concern                      sricha l'gufa. Rav Moshe: Permitted - genuine
                             danger to Jewish people if Jewish doctors don't
p. 23014. Refuah — Medical Treatment
Scenario                       Ruling

                               treat non-Jews.

Karaite (observes              Magen Avraham citing Knesses Gedolah:
Shabbos)                       Permitted to break Shabbos.

Tinok shenishba                Permitted - treated like a Jew.


Eighth-Month Baby
   • Based on Rishonim: Permitted to break Shabbos only if hair and nails fully
      developed.
   • Contemporary ruling: Obligatory to perform Melachos for any premature
      baby - modern medicine can save them.


Putting Oneself in a Situation of Danger
   • Forbidden to place oneself in a situation where one will definitely need to
      do Melachos on Shabbos (Baal HaMeor; Mechaber).
   • Baal HaMeor: Forbidden only within 3 days of Shabbos; permitted more
      than 3 days before. Permitted within 3 days for a Mitzva.
   • Biur Halacha: Many Rishonim disagree - forbidden any day of the week.
      Conclusion: be strict.
   • Rav Moshe: Even if one unjustifiably placed himself in danger - still
      obligated to break Shabbos to save him.


Returning After Saving a Life (Hitiru Sofan Mishum Haschalasan)
   • If the rescuer is still needed at his original place (e.g., Hatzala): Permitted
      to do Issurei doraisa (drive) to return.
   • If not needed: Most Poskim permit Issurei derabanan (e.g., ask non-Jew to
      drive) but not doraisa.
   • Rav Moshe Feinstein: Permits Issurei doraisa if he expected to complete
     the task and return within Shabbos.
   • Rav Tzvi Pesach Frank (and most Poskim): Does not permit Issurei doraisa
     to return unless he may be needed for further pikuach nefesh.
p. 23114. Refuah — Medical Treatment

p. 23215. Kosher U'Matir — Tying & Untying
                   Kosher U'Matir


1. Background: The Melacha of Kosher

Source in the Mishkan                     Thread ends were knotted to hold
                                          stitching in place; seam ends were
                                          knotted to prevent unraveling.


Melacha of Matir                          Untying is the corresponding
                                          melacha (mirror of Kosher).

4. Mechaber and Rama - Halacha L'Maaseh

Mechaber (SA 317:1)                Rules like Rif/Rambam: only a
                                   permanent kesher uman is assur
                                   mid'oraisa.


Rama                               Combines both opinions (strict on
                                   each point): • A permanent knot =
                                   assur mid'oraisa even if not a
                                   kesher uman (Rashi). • A kesher
                                   uman made to untie that day =
                                   assur mid'rabanan (Rif/Rambam).
                                   • Two opinions cited: knot
                                   permitted if < 1 week OR only if
                                   untied same day - halacha is to be
                                   strict: only permitted if untied
                                   same day.

6. Twist-Ties, Ropes, and Cutting

Twisting into a rope (Rambam)      Making threads into a rope is a
                                   tolda of Kosher; undoing it is a
                                   tolda of Matir - even without an
                                   actual knot, if it creates a very tight
                                   binding.


Twist-tie (Rav S.Z. Auerbach)      Twisting more than once and
                                   leaving closed for more than one
                                   day is forbidden. Twisting once
                                   only = permitted.


Cutting a permitted knot           Permitted (equivalent to untying).
                                   Should not be done in front of an
                                   am ha'aretz.


Cutting a forbidden knot           Forbidden.


Knots on choslos (vessel           Permitted to untie or cut - these
wrapping)                          are not made-to-last knots
                                   (Mishnah Berurah).
p. 23815. Kosher U'Matir — Tying & Untying
7. Melacha of Matir - Untying

Authority       Position                     Condition


Rach            Chayav only if untying in    Must have intent to re-tie
                order to re-tie (matir al
                menas likshor)


Tosefos         Uncertain                    -


Rashi           Chayav even if not al        No condition required
                menas likshor


Biur Halacha    Assur mid'oraisa to untie    Positive benefit required
                any otherwise-forbidden      (e.g. to open a vessel)
                knot if there is any
                positive benefit to the
                untying




Poskim: It is always permitted to untie any knot that was made
inadvertently - whether made on Shabbos or on a weekday.




8. Tying for the Sake of a Mitzva

The Question                        May one tie a knot that is normally
                                    forbidden (assur mid'rabanan) if
                                    doing so is needed for a mitzva?
p. 23915. Kosher U'Matir — Tying & Untying
Rambam / Tur / Mechaber            Permitted to tie a normally assur
                                   mid'rabanan knot for the sake of a
                                   mitzva.


Rashi / Tosefos / Bartenura        Strict - not permitted even for a
                                   mitzva.


Mishnah Berurah                    Implies to be strict. Exception:
                                   fixing a broken eruv on Shabbos
                                   to prevent the public from sinning
                                   (mitzva d'rabbim).


Rav Moshe Feinstein                Lenient for a mitzva d'rabbim (e.g.
                                   lights in a shul so the tzibbur can
                                   daven/learn).


Rav Elyashiv                       Strict even for a mitzva d'rabbim.


Melacha doraisa for mitzva         Generally forbidden. In the Beis
                                   HaMikdash only: even doraisa
                                   permitted to fix instruments
                                   (Rambam).




Shvus d'shvus: Asking a non-Jew (shvus #1) to do an issur
derabanan (shvus #2) is permitted for a mitzva, great need, or
miksas choli - but that is amira l'akum, not Kosher itself.
p. 24015. Kosher U'Matir — Tying & Untying

p. 24116. Tofer U'Koraya — Sewing & Tearing
                     Tofer U'Koraya

1. Background: The Melacha of Tofer

Source in the Mishkan               The ten panels of the bottom wool
                                    covering were sewn together.
                                    Alternatively (Yerushalmi): sewing
                                    was needed to repair torn
                                    coverings.


Core definition                     Weaving/sewing together parts of
                                    fabric into one combined unit.


Koraya - the mirror melacha         Tearing apart what was sewn
                                    together. Discussed in Sections 4–
                                    7 below.

3. Tofer L'Zman - Is Temporary Sewing
Permitted?

The Question: Just as a temporary knot (Kosher l'zman) is
permitted, is a temporary act of sewing (Tofer l'zman) also
permitted?




Authority        Position                       Notes


Mordechi         Strict - no heter for          Mechaber rules like
                 temporary Tofer                Mordechi (SA 340:6–7)


Ravya            Lenient - temporary Tofer      Minhag followed this
                 is permitted, just like        (Darchei Moshe)
                 temporary Kosher


Mechaber         Strict - rules like
(SA 340)         Mordechi; does not cite
                 Ravya


Rama (SA         Appears strict (like           Chazon Ish: Rama is
p. 24316. Tofer U'Koraya — Sewing & Tearing
340:7)           Mordechi)                     strict


Rama (SA         Permits relying on Ravya      Rav S.Z. Auerbach:
317:3)           - not in front of amei        Rama is lenient
                 ha'aretz


Tehilla          Strict for temporary Tofer;   Hybrid position
L'David / Rav    lenient for temporary
Elyashiv         Koraya (tearing)


Beis Yosef       Permits relying on Ravya      Darchei Moshe HaAruch
(SA 317)         - but not in front of amei    agrees
                 ha'aretz




Bottom line: The Poskim dispute the Rama's position. L'maaseh,
one should not rely on the leniency in front of amei ha'aretz. The
Minhag was to follow the Ravya.


Tightening a Loosened Stitch (SA 340:6)

loosened stitch                      Mechaber) - because of Tofer. If
                                     there is also a knot, transgresses
                                     mid'oraisa even more clearly.


Garment designed to be               Permitted - it is recognizable that

                                     designed; does not appear as
                                     tightening a thread (Mordechi).


Two stitches (no knot)               Assur mid'oraisa to tighten - Pri
                                     Megadim: becomes very tight
                                     even without a knot.

                                     Moshe OC 2:84).

5. The Melacha of Koraya - Definition
Basic definition                 Tearing apart what was
                                 sewn/joined together - the mirror
                                 melacha of Tofer.


Rambam (Shabbos 10:11)           Sticking together pieces of paper
                                 or skin = tolda of Tofer. Tearing
                                 them apart = Koraya.


What requires Koraya?            Tearing apart items that were
                                 previously combined into one unit.
p. 24616. Tofer U'Koraya — Sewing & Tearing
Does Koraya Apply to Paper and Skin?

Authority      Position                    Basis


Shulchan       Koraya only applies to      Logical derivation from
Aruch HaRav    materials that were         Tofer/Koraya relationship
(340:17a)      originally made of
               separate pieces that were
               combined. Paper and
               skin - never separate
               sections - are NOT
               subject to Koraya.


Biur Halacha   Disagrees - tearing skin    Yerushalmi
(340:13)       IS Koraya, per the
               Yerushalmi.


Rambam         Tearing paper =             Gemara, Beitzah
(Shabbos       forbidden due to Tikkun
23:6)          Maneh (a form of Makeh
               V'Patish) - does NOT
               mention Koraya.
p. 24716. Tofer U'Koraya — Sewing & Tearing
6. Koraya Al Menas Litfor - Must One Intend to
Re-Sew?
The Question: Is Koraya mid'oraisa only when tearing in order to
sew back (al menas litfor), or even for any constructive purpose?
All agree: purely destructive tearing is not assur mid'oraisa.


Authority       Position                       Notes


Gemara          One who tears as an act        Constructive tearing =
(Shabbos        of mourning or out of          chayav even without litfor
105b)           anger is chayav - even
                without intent to re-sew.


Rashi (105b)    Tearing as an act of
                mourning = Melacha
                she'ein tzricha l'gufo - not
                mid'oraisa.


Tosefos         Tearing for mourning =         Machloket between Rashi
(105b)          she'tzricha l'gufo             and Tosefos
                (chayav). Tearing out of
                anger = she'ein tzricha
                l'gufo.


Biur Halacha    Any constructive tearing =     Main practical ruling
(340)           assur mid'oraisa, even
                without intent to re-sew.


Biur Halacha    Koraya requires intent to      Explains why tearing
- further       use both parts of the torn     paper for roasting fish is
refinement      item. If only one part is      not Koraya
                used and the other
                discarded - no Koraya.
                But the usable part
                triggers Makeh V'Patish.
p. 24816. Tofer U'Koraya — Sewing & Tearing
7. Koraya of Vessels and Packaging
Breaking a barrel (Mishna 146a)      Permitted - Rashi: destructive act.
                                     Tosefos: barrel is unstable, liable
                                     to fall apart on its own; breaking it
                                     is not real Soser. Ran: small
                                     vessel - only mid'rabanan;
                                     permitted for Shabbos need.


Tearing skin covering of a barrel    Permitted - Rav Moshe Feinstein:
                                     Koraya only applies when the torn
                                     item will visibly be sewn up again.
                                     If there is no visible evidence of
                                     constructive use, it is permitted.


Choslos (date-leaf fruit             Permitted to cut open - Mechaber:
wrapping)                            treated like peels.


Food packets discarded after         Permitted - Rav Moshe: wrapping
use                                  designed only for that one use =
                                     treated like a peel; no Issur.


Food packets that are reused         Forbidden to tear - the peel-
                                     analogy does not apply.


Rav Moshe's Gezeira: Despite the above heteirim, Rav Moshe
issued a general prohibition against opening packets, vessels,
and boxes on Shabbos. This ruling is not universally followed.
The Poskim recommend opening all such items before Shabbos to
avoid the issue entirely.




Chazon Ish: Strict - some Poskim say: immediately discard the
packet after opening to satisfy the Chazon Ish's concern.
p. 24916. Tofer U'Koraya — Sewing & Tearing
8. Separating Stuck Pages

Pages stuck together                Permitted to separate - Magen
inadvertently (food, substance)     Avraham: kal v'chomer from the
                                    fact that intentionally tied
                                    temporary knots may be untied.


Pages stuck together with           Forbidden - tearing erases writing
writing on the edges                (Mochek).


Pages stuck together at binding     Forbidden - tearing them open =
(never separated at production)     Makeh V'Patish (fixing/completing
                                    the item).

p. 25117. Memachek — Smoothing
                          Memachek

1. Foundations - Definition of Memachek

Memachek ('smoothing') is one of the 39 Melachos. Its origin in the Mishkan was
smoothing the hides used in construction.


Memachek vs. Gozez - What's the Difference?
View                    Distinction Between Memachek & Gozez

Rambam (Shabbos         Gozez = removing hair/wool for the sake of the
11:5, 9:7)              hair/wool itself. Memachek = removing hair for the
                        sake of the skin - to smooth it.

Sidrei Tahara (citing   The method differs: Gozez = cutting. Memachek =
Rash)                   scraping.


Can Memachek Apply to a Living Animal?
The Rambam implies Memachek only applies post-mortem. However, Tosefos
(Shabbos 73b) disagrees: Rabbeinu Tam held that milking an animal is Memachek
(because the nipples are smoothed). Tosefos did not accept that application but
agreed Memachek can in principle occur on a living animal.


Surfaces Beyond Animal Hides
Source                  Application

Gemara Shabbos 75b      Smoothing the ground between pillars of a building =
(Rashi)                 Memachek.

Rambam / Tosefos        Rubbing the leather stretched over pillars to smooth it
(Shabbos 75b)           = Memachek.

Gemara Shabbos          Removing hairs from a bird's spine is Memachek only
p. 25217. Memachek — Smoothing
Source                  Application

74b; Chayei Adam        if intent is for the skin. If for the hair - not Memachek.

   Key       One is only liable for Memachek when the intent is for the sake of
Principle    the surface being smoothed - not for the material being removed.



2. Memarayach - Smoothing Soft Substances

Memarayach is the Tolda (sub-category) of Memachek that applies to soft and
pliable substances - as opposed to the Av Melacha which involves hard surfaces.
The Mishna (Shabbos 146a) establishes that smearing wax into a barrel opening
is Assur midoraisa.


Three Levels of Substance Consistency
Type                Status              Examples

Pliant solid        Assur midoraisa     Wax, solid soap, chapstick, solid
substances (hard                        lipstick, solid deodorant, tar,
enough to hold                          congealed fat, dough, Silly Putty.
shape)

Dense semi-solids   Assur               Facial/hand creams, petroleum jelly,
(thick but          miderabanan         skin cream, toothpaste.
spreadable)

Viscous liquids     Generally           Liquid soap (most Poskim permit; Rav
(flows freely)      permitted           Berkovits and Rav Moshe are strict),
                    (some Poskim        baby oil, olive oil.
                    strict if it
                    lathers)
p. 25317. Memachek — Smoothing
Key Practical Cases
Case                          Ruling

Pressing/shaping soft wax     Assur midoraisa (also Muktza).
drippings

Melting bottom of wax         Assur midoraisa - even on Yom Tov.
candle to stick to holder

Chapstick for chapped lips    Assur midoraisa (also possible Issur refuah).

Solid lipstick                Assur midoraisa (also Tzovaya).

Solid deodorant sticks        Assur midoraisa.

Washing with solid soap       Assur midoraisa - all contemporary Ashkenazic
                              Poskim. Sefardim: Ohr Letsion forbids; Rav
                              Ovadiah permits (praiseworthy to be strict).

Facial/hand creams,           Assur miderabanan.
petroleum jelly

                              Berurah; accepted minhag). Sefardim: Ohr
                              Letsion forbids; Rav Ovadiah permits if needed
                              for health.

Medicinal cream on infant's   Permitted - may press it on (not smear) if the
rash                          child is a Choleh she'ein bo sakana. Also
                              permitted under a diaper, spread by the baby's
                              movement.

Liquid soap                   Most Poskim permit (incl. Rav Elyashiv). Rav
                              Moshe and Rav Berkovits are strict. Can be
                              diluted with water on one's hand to satisfy the
                              strict view.

Baby oil / olive oil          Permitted.

Stepping on saliva on the     Permitted - intent is for it to be absorbed, not
ground                        smoothed. If one intends to smooth it:
                              forbidden.

to holder                       touching wax lest one smooth it.



3. Memachek B'Ochlin - Smoothing Foods

The Rishonim and Acharonim debate whether Memachek applies to foods at all,
and if so, to what degree.


Status             Conditions                      Source / Basis

Assur midoraisa    Smoothing food for a non-       The food is being used as a
                   food purpose (e.g., plugging    building material - full
                   a crack with chewing gum        Memachek applies.
                   or sticky candy).

Assur              Food that is inedible           Magen Avraham (SA 321, sk
miderabanan        without being smoothed.         24); Mordechai.

Permitted          Food is edible without          Rama (SA 321:19); Magen
                   smoothing; intent is simply     Avraham; Biur Halacha.
                   to spread it to all areas.

Permitted, but     Food is edible without          Mordechai; Rama:
praiseworthy to    smoothing; intent is            'Hamachmir tavo alav
be strict          aesthetic (to make it thin or   bracha.' Biur Halacha: this
                   decorative).                    only applies when intent is
                                                   for aesthetic thinning, not
                                                   spreading.

chewing gum or sticky           not food.

              The key questions: (1) Is the substance solid, semi-solid, or liquid?
 Bottom       (2) Is the intent to smooth a surface, or merely to spread/cover?

              smoothing purely aesthetic?
p. 25718. Boneh, Soser, Makeh Bipatesh & Ohel
    Boneh, Soser V'Makeh V'Patish


                        PART A: BONEH



1. Background & Shiur

Source in the Mishkan          The walls of the Mishkan were
                               formed by assembling specially
                               designed wooden planks.
                               Assembling them = the Melacha of
                               Boneh.


Shiur for chiyuv               Kol shehu - the minimum possible
                               amount (Mishna, Shabbos 102b).
                               Even a tiny act of building creates
                               chiyuv, as long as it can last.


Examples of Boneh              Filling in a hole in a dirt floor,
                               leveling the ground, making a wall.
p. 25818. Boneh, Soser, Makeh Bipatesh & Ohel
2. Building a Wall - Machlokes Rishonim

Authority        Bottom stone (no             Top layer (no cement)
                 cement)


Rashi +          CHAYAV - no cement           CHAYAV - stable even
Tosefos          needed; straightening into   without cement
                 place suffices


Ramban           Not assur mid'oraisa         Not assur mid'oraisa


Rambam           Not Boneh doraisa -          Not chayav unless
                 would be Makeh V'Patish      cement under it



3. Mosif Al HaBinyan - Adding to an Existing
Building

Permanent addition                  FORBIDDEN - Mosif al habinyan;
                                    appears as adding a foreign object
                                    to the structure.


Bolt/peg inserted temporarily       Must be planned before Shabbos
(condition 1)                       to insert. Normally removed and
                                    replaced.


Bolt/peg inserted temporarily       May not be intended to remain
(condition 2)                       permanently. If permanent: must
                                    be attached by string/rope.


Foreign material inserted (e.g.     PERMITTED even without pre-
clothing)                           planning - not the normal function
                                    of the window.
p. 25918. Boneh, Soser, Makeh Bipatesh & Ohel
4. Mechitsa Arai - Temporary Walls

Authority       Mechitsa for                Mechitsa Hamateres
                Tznius/Kavod                (enables carrying etc.)


Rashi           PERMITTED                   PERMITTED


Tosefos         PERMITTED                   FORBIDDEN
                                            (mid'rabanan)


Mechaber /      PERMITTED                   FORBIDDEN
Rama (SA
315:1)


Chazon Ish      FORBIDDEN if hung           -
                permanently




Permitted: curtain in front of a door (tznius); Paroches of an Aron
Kodesh; wall to block sun/wind/candles. Forbidden: Mechitsa
hamateres; wall for marital purposes in front of a candle (Rama).
p. 26018. Boneh, Soser, Makeh Bipatesh & Ohel
5. Unblocking a Drain or Toilet on Shabbos

Gemara (Kesubos 60a)              Assur mid'oraisa to unblock a pipe
                                  normally; permitted with a shinui
                                  (unusual manner) in private, in a
                                  case of loss.


Shevisas HaShabbos                Unblocking normally = Boneh -
                                  makes the pipe usable again.


Be'er Moshe                       Severely blocked pipe = assur
                                  mid'oraisa. Toilet/sink: a minor
                                  blockage is not significant -
                                  permitted even normally and even
                                  with a plunger.


Chelkas Yaakov                    Unblocking a drain = issur
                                  derabanan of Tikkun Maneh -
                                  permitted for kavod habriyos.


Rav Moshe Feinstein               Strict: only permits if the drain
                                  clogs very commonly. If totally
                                  blocked - ask a non-Jew in great
                                  need.




Bottom line: Many poskim permit unblocking a toilet/sink in a time
of need. Rav Moshe is strict.
p. 26118. Boneh, Soser, Makeh Bipatesh & Ohel
                 PART B: BINYAN B'KEILIM



6. The Core Machlokes: Ein vs. Yesh Binyan
B'Keilim

The Question: Does the Melacha of Boneh apply to assembling
vessels (keilim), or only to structures attached to the ground?




Authority        Position                    Basis / Limits


Rashi            EIN binyan b'keilim -       Only building
                 Boneh never applies to      houses/shelters = Boneh;
                 any kli (under 40 seah)     kli > 40 seah IS subject to
                                             Boneh


Tosefos          YESH binyan b'keilim -      Only reassembling (not
                 building a new kli can be   building anew) = Ein
                 Boneh mid'oraisa            binyan. Applies only to
                                             'binyan gamur'


Halacha          Follows Tosefos - Ein       Building a kli anew or in a
                 binyan b'keilim applies     very firm manner = Yesh
                 only to minor/reassembly    binyan b'keilim




The 40-seah rule: All agree that a kli holding 40+ seah is not
considered a 'kli' for halacha - full Issur Boneh doraisa applies to
it (Rashi; Eruvin 34b).
p. 26218. Boneh, Soser, Makeh Bipatesh & Ohel
7. The Three Levels of Tightness in Assembling a
Kli

Derech Rafui                         Weak/loose connection. Kol Bo:
                                     parts move in the hole. Smag
                                     (halacha): easy to separate the
                                     parts - even tight grooves if easily
                                     pressed apart.


Derech Mehudak                       Firm/moderate connection. Smag:
                                     strength or expertise needed to
                                     separate. Magen Avraham:
                                     screwing = takua. Taz: screwing =
                                     mehudak.


Derech Takua                         Very strong, peg-like connection -
                                     parts are fully locked into place.




Halacha by Level of Tightness

Normal         Assembling       Assembling           Assembling
derech of      b'derech rafui   b'derech             b'derech takua
this kli                        mehudak


Normally       PERMITTED        -                     -
rafui          (all)


Normally       PERMITTED for    FORBIDDEN             -
mehudak        Shabbos need     unless sorech
               (MB) Chazon      gadol (SA
               Ish: always      HaRav)
               permitted
p. 26318. Boneh, Soser, Makeh Bipatesh & Ohel

takua         (Hagahos Ashri;                     MID'ORAISA
              MB)
              PERMITTED
              (Rosh; Chazon
              Ish)




Key practical rule: Screwing the lid of a baby bottle or kli =
PERMITTED. The Chazon Ish and Rav Karelitz: opening/closing is
the kli's regular shimush - not Boneh at all.




Lego: Rafui (Rav Auerbach). Permitted for children. Adults -
forbidden (may be building a new structure). High-chair tray with
easy-press groove = rafui = permitted.

The Rif's three-part stringency: (1) Ohel with roof ≥ 1 tefach =
assur mid'oraisa even if temporary. (2) Roof < 1 tefach = still assur
mid'rabanan. (3) Pre-attached string only helps if roof < 1 tefach.
The Mechaber follows the Rif.

                     1. Tzovaya (Dyeing)


A. Tzovaya L'Zman - Temporary Dyeing

Category                      Ruling


Permanent coloring            Assur mid'oraisa


Temporary coloring (fades     Assur mid'rabanan
on its own, short time)


If color is easily removed    Assur mid'rabanan


Color intended to be          Smag: assur mid'oraisa. Rambam / Mechaber:
temporary - machlokes         assur mid'rabanan. Halacha follows Rambam.


No Tzovaya mid'oraisa on      Because color is not absorbed - only issur
human skin                    derabanan for cosmetics


Cases

Cosmetics (rouge, lipstick,   Assur mid'rabanan - temporary effect
eyeshadow)


Talcum powder on skin         Machlokes: Rav Moshe & Rav Scheinberg -
                              muttar; RSZ Auerbach & Rav Wosner - assur
                              mid'rabanan


Water paint on glass/metal    Assur mid'rabanan - easily wiped


Crayon on formica/metal       Assur mid'rabanan
p. 27619. Various — Part 1
B. Tzovaya b'Ochlin - Staining with Food / Wiping Stains

Opinion              Position


Yeraim               Assur mid'rabanan to wipe a stain with cloth (psik reisha
                     d'loh nichah leih); forbids covering wound with clothing


Radbaz / Agur        Permitted - Derech lichluch (abnormal way)


Magen Avraham        Rules like Yeraim; same-color cloth is certainly
                     forbidden


Mishnah Berurah /    Ideally follow Yeraim; avoid same-color cloth; wash
Elyah Rabbah         blood off first if possible


Shemiras Shabbos     Permitted to use disposable paper towel or tissue
/ Rav Ribiat


Rav Berkovits        Permits rag used specifically for stains; not a regular
                     hand towel

Case                Ruling


Color-changing      RSZ Auerbach: lenient in case of need (very temporary,
thermometer         nothing new added). If letters appear - depends on
                    whether outline was pre-existing.


Photochromic        Most Poskim permit: part of normal function, very
(darkening)         temporary, possibly indirect (gramma factor)
glasses


Sunbathing /        Shemiras Shabbos: permitted; Minchas Yitzchak:
p. 27719. Various — Part 1
getting a tan         forbidden. Walking in sun without intent - permitted to all.


Colored toilet        Tzitz Eliezer, Ohr L'Tzion, Rav Ovadia: lenient (psik

                      Auerbach, Rav Wosner, Orchos Shabbos: remove before
                      Shabbos. If not removed - kavod habrios considerations
                      apply.

Poisonous / life-             Permitted to kill - even if not presently chasing
threatening (e.g., rabid
dog, poisonous snake,
scorpion)


Causes significant pain       Permitted to kill
but not life-threatening,
presently pursuing


Causes significant pain,      Only permitted to step on inconspicuously
not pursuing


Causes some pain (e.g.,       Forbidden to kill outright; permitted to trap or step
non-poisonous hornet)         on
p. 27819. Various — Part 1

                             spray perimeter if in kitchen.


Lice                         SA: permitted (do not reproduce normally).
                             Modern lice do reproduce - Rav Dessler & RSZ

                             causing pain to child).

Which melacha?               Rashi/Tosefos: Netilas Neshama. Rambam:
                             Dosh. Halacha follows Rashi/Tosefos.


Chiyuv requires              Constructive purpose (e.g., feeding animal,
                             weakening it, Rambam: even anger)


Hitting with anger           Rambam: assur mid'oraisa. Raavad: assur
                             mid'rabanan.


Psik reisha - no benefit     Assur mid'rabanan
from bleeding


Cases

bleed

bleed

                             pain - ask non-Jew.

Blood test on Shabbos          Assur mid'oraisa; only permitted for pikuach

                     3. Tzod (Trapping)
                             Confining an animal




A. Mino Nitzod vs. Ein B'Mino Nitzod

Category                        Examples / Halacha


Mino nitzod (commonly           Rabbits (fur/food), parrots (pets). Trapping =
trapped)                        issur d'oraisa with narrow confinement.


Ein b'mino nitzod (not          Flies. Trapping = assur mid'rabanan only.
commonly confined)


Honey bees - machlokes          Beis Yosef: Mino nitzod. Most Poskim: Ein
                                b'mino nitzod (beekeeper fosters, not truly
                                traps).


B. Levels of Confinement

Narrow confinement              Assur mid'oraisa


Loose confinement               Assur mid'rabanan


Further confining already-      Permitted as long as does not reach narrow
loosely-confined animal         confinement
p. 28019. Various — Part 1
Adequacy of confinement        Must match the animal - a dog's cage is
                               inadequate for a lion; high walls trap dogs but
                               not birds




C. Trapping Flies - Halacha L'Maaseh

Case                       Ruling


Intentionally trapping a   Assur mid'rabanan (fly = ein b'mino nitzod)
fly


Closing small box with     Tur: permits (hard to catch fly even from small
fly inside                 box). Sefer HaTerumah: forbids. Mishnah Berurah:
                           strict like Sefer HaTerumah.


Closing large box with     All agree: permitted (too loose to be meaningful
fly inside                 confinement)


Unsure if fly is in box    Taz: permits. Mishnah Berurah: permits (only
(safek psik reisha)        d'rabanan concern). Chazon Ish: strict.


D. Trapping Harmful Animals - Halacha L'Maaseh

Category                   Ruling


Life-threatening animals   Permitted to trap (and kill - see Section 2A)


Animals causing            Permitted to trap
considerable pain


Animals causing some       Permitted to hold and throw; forbidden to trap if not
pain, on person's body     on body


Insects causing            Rav Karelitz: permitted to trap. RSZ Auerbach:
discomfort / preventing    forbidden. Ask a Rav.
sleep

                 7. Hachana (Preparation)
                Preparing on Shabbos for after Shabbos




A. Core Rules

Hachana is forbidden because it constitutes unnecessary tircha on Shabbos for
a weekday purpose.

The issur applies equally to preparing on Shabbos for after Shabbos, on Yom
Tov Rishon for Yom Tov Sheini, and on Shabbos for Yom Tov.

Actions that have a benefit for Shabbos itself are permitted even if they also
benefit after Shabbos.


Case                                  Ruling


Making bed for kavod Shabbos          Permitted - benefit for Shabbos


Washing dishes to be used later       Permitted
on Shabbos


Washing dishes (not needed            Many Poskim permit if it would be
again on Shabbos)                     unpleasant to leave dirty dishes visible


Washing dishes primarily to           Forbidden
avoid post-Shabbos cleanup


Washing ten dishes when only          Permitted
one is needed


Soaking dishes on Shabbos             Discussed separately - depends on
                                      circumstances
p. 29119. Various — Part 1
B. Hachana - Folding and Preparing Clothing

Case                        Ruling


Folding clothing on an      Mechaber: permitted (even if won't wear again
irregular fold              Shabbos). Chayei Adam: strict.


Folding tallis on Yom       Elyah Rabbah: requires Eiruv Tavshilin. R' Akiva
Tov for Shabbos             Eiger: lenient even without.


Preparing from Yom Tov      Forbidden unless Eiruv Tavshilin was made
for Shabbos                 (machloket - see Ran/Magen Avraham)




C. Hachana - Special Cases

Case                              Ruling


Taking medication before          Orchos Shabbos: permitted - effect begins
Shabbos for post-Shabbos          Shabbos itself; if mixed in food, not obvious
effect


Learning for a test in limmudei   Permitted - benefit even now
kodesh


Learning for test in limmudei     Rav Auerbach: permitted if genuinely wants
chol                              to know material; unsure if purely to pass
                                  test


Looking for Sefer Torah on        Mishnah Berurah: forbidden - hachana
Shabbos for next-day Yom Tov
p. 29219. Various — Part 1

Berurah

(tunefully)

Doorknocker      Mutar l'chatchila
(Sefard)

Torah crown      Mitzva). Shaarei Ephraim: ideally strict, no need to rebuke
                 lenient. Rav Wosner: modern bells so quiet - mutar l'all.

B. Avsha Milsa - Activating Noisy Appliances Before
Shabbos

Issur: Causing noisy vessels (e.g., washing machine, dryer, dishwasher) to
operate on Shabbos.

The concern: people will think the melacha was done on Shabbos.


Case                              Ruling


Washing machine / dryer /         Forbidden. Rav Ben-Tzion Abba Shaul:
dishwasher set to run on          forbidden even by Mechaber's standard.
Shabbos


Refrigerator (always on,          Permitted - everyone knows it runs
many days)                        continuously


Timer air conditioning (on/off    Rav Elyashiv: forbidden. If on/off more than
every few hours)                  daily cycle: permitted. In great discomfort:
                                  permitted regardless.


Alarm clock                       Most Poskim: permit even if heard by others.
                                  Rav Moshe Feinstein: forbidden if heard by
                                  others.


Generator to prevent Chillul      Permitted - even though noisy
Shabbos
